Pools are private and very well maintained.The Sites: DON'T TAKE A CAB. Outside hotel is Bus Stop (PARADA) and take B21 bus into Old San Juan. cost is 75 cents and very safe. I prepare to leave feeling that although the Condado Hotel and Casino has what it takes to be 4-5 stars I wonder if they are committed to providing that level of service.The Bars: B-. Seriously, it's worth doing.The Bill: B+. Check your bill as I had extra fees to remove regarding valet parking when no one visited and I didn't have a car. Overall cost was ok as I travel alot and adjusted quickly.I would return since i know the ins and outs of the hotel and what and what not to pay for.

<Author>cattom
<Content>Beautiful ocean view at the Condado Plaza We vacationed at the Condado Plaza for 10 days in early December, and were very happy to have done so. The view from the Oceanview room is absolutely magnificent, and it is definitely worth the extra cost versus staying on the Cityside. First, the positive:-Magnificent ocean view in room-Contemporary rooms with modern furniture-Two pools with excellent poolside service- Gym with state-of-the-art equipment- Strip House restaurant on premises is beautiful with a fantastic ocean view and excellent food and service- it was the best steak dinner we have ever had, and we are from the NY Metro area, where restaurants abound. It is somewhat expensive, though.- Many good restaurants on Ashford Avenue within walking distance- Ropa Vieja, Anjuli Mojili, Budatai (excellent), and lots of good sushi places nearby. There is also a Chile鈥檚 on Ashford Avenue if you want a quick and inexpensive meal. The Italian restaurant at the Condado is adequate, and there is also a good view. Starbucks is just outside the front door. -Hotel is close to Old San Juan-Staff is efficient and friendly-Easy, fast, polite check-in and check-out-Any problems are quickly handled by Customer Relations Manager, Henry Neumann- we had a noisy air conditioner the first night, and complained twice to the front desk. They immediately notified maintenance, but they did not respond. We notified Mr. Neumann, who quickly took care of it. He is quite responsive, efficient, and professional, and is an asset to the Condado Plaza. My husband had a toothache during our stay, and Mr. Neumann arranged for us to see a local dentist. He does what is takes to make your stay at the Condado pleasant and stress-free. I highly recommend contacting him should you have any problems that are not being resolved by the front desk.Negatives-Casino is packed almost all of the time, as it is popular with many local Puerto Ricans as well as hotel guests.-Surrounding area has a lot of construction, and some buildings have not been finished due to poor economy.-Odd bathroom set-up with coffeemaker and closet in bathroom and no lock on door.-Very small beach, not really used by hotel occupants -City-like surroundings- if you like being in a country -type, away- from-it- all setting, this hotel is not for you. However, it appears to be quite safe, with joggers going down Ashford Avenue all times of the day and night.All in all, we liked our vacation experience, and will return to the Condado Plaza.

<Author>Sapper123
<Content>Amiable Stay at Condado Plaza Stayed at the Condado Plaza for four nights in early Dec 2008. We had a large room with a nice, unobstructed view of the lagoon. Unlike other reviews, I found the reception/front desk friendly and professional. Did not eat at any of the hotel's restaurants, but there are many. Pools are nice, but the beach area is small and, upon entering the water, rather rocky. The water is calm though since you are more in a lagoon rather than the Atlantic. There are also some bridge repairs taking place adjacent to the beach and if they are driving piles for the bridge's foundation, then it can be noisy. Close to Old San Juan and other hotels/boutiques (Cartier, Gucci) on the Condado strip. Housekeeping was efficient, but not necessarily all encompasing. Bellman service was also polite and quick, but missed little things (i.e. placing luggage on luggage stand). Efficiency wise, if you self park, you have to validate the parking ticket everytime you go out. Wish they would just provide you with a special ticket that allows you to come and go as you please without having to waste time validating a ticket. Also, be aware of resort fees, island taxes, and city taxes. They will likely make up about 25-30% of your final bill.

<Author>Saamson
<Content>Simply the best As I write this, I am sitting in my ocean front room at this wonderful hotel on Nov 21, 2008. I just want to let everyone know that this hotel is the best hotel I have ever stayed at. The rooms are exceptionally clean and decorated with a beautiful modern decor. The bathroom has to be one of the nicest bathrooms I have ever seen anywhere, let alone a hotel room. There is a shower right in the middle of the bathroom that is all encased in a glass enclosure which is a set up I will be copying in my own master bathroom. Even the toiletries that are provided are of top notch quality and comparable to any expensive brand name. And to boot, the cleaning service takes the time to clean your room thoroughly and carefully place items that are out of place back to where they should be. Simply put, you must see the room for yourself to really get an appreciation of the focus on detail that was put into the decoration and set up of the entire room. As for the rest hotel, it just keeps getting better. In the lobby level there is a bar that just isn't a simple old bar. It's comparable to some of the nicest bars/clubs that I've seen over in South Beach. The bartender that was on duty that night (monday) was a guy named Lance who was everything you would like to see in a resort bartender; funny, knowledgeable of the area and other vacation spots in the world, and his personality simply just made our night. I believe he said he was just getting back in to bar tending and working just one night that week. If I were the manager of that bar, I would hire him on a permanent basis in a heartbeat. And if you don't want to be inside and listen to the music that is playing, there is an expansive covered porch area facing the ocean where you have the freedom to walk around and sit wherever you please. Now for the pool area...There are 2 different pools. One huge 3 foot deep pool that wraps around the building with lights that change colors during the evening, and full bar that serves the pool with wait staff that will bring you your drink or food right to you with the nicest similes and personality in the world, and to boot has a volleyball net and a very slick water slide that my wife seemed to taken a loving too. The food is very reasonably priced and very good. Then there is a 6 foot deep salt water pool !!! As for the beach, it is somewhat of a lagoon set up that is protected by large rocks roughly 400 feet away from the beach so that the waves aren't too hard to handle and anyone (including my wife who can't swim) can enjoy the ocean water safely. Going back to the wait staff, we ordered food by the pool and asked them if it would be ok to eat the food by our chairs on the beach. They smiled and said not only can you eat there we will bring the food out to you. I was floored. And again, it gets better. We looked over to a gazebo by the right side of the beach and saw a guy standing there with what looked like a massage station. My wife and I walked over and asked the gentleman what we did, and he said he was a massage therapist. Well when we heard that, we absolutely had to take advantage of that. My wife went first and then me 2nd. Just think to yourself... You're getting a massage from a professional, under a gazebo over looking the ocean, with the sounds of the Caribbean all around you. It just doesn't get any better than that. Once we went back into the ocean we ran into a few other people who were also from NJ. Everyone one of them were also impressed with the place and had perma smiles on their faces. The experience just keeps getting better and better. I can't comment on the Casino because I don't gamble, but if the casino is anything like the rest of the hotel it just has to be another enjoyable part of the place. All in all I have to say that if you're looking forward to booking a trip to Puerto Rico, you must stay at the Condado. The Ritz, La Concha and Condado Plaza are the 3 gems of San Juan. The people who left negative reviews about this place have to be the types of people who complain no matter where they go even if they stay at the Waldorf in NYC because there is no way a hotel can do any better that what Condado has done for my wife, me and my friends this past week. The Condado and it's staff have given us memories that will certainly last us a lifetime. If you have any further questions about my simply remarkable experience in San Juan and my stay at the Condado, please feel free to email me at saamson@gmail.com. I will more that glad to help you with your trip.

<Content>I'd give the Condado a C+ I recently returned from a 3-day stay at the Condado with my girlfriend  another couple. The hotel itself is nice, clean, and stylish. The color scheme, the shower, etc.... all very unique.- The room was cleaned in a timely fashion. - Room service was solid. The breakfast was good, came on time, and was not too expensive.- The balcony in the room looking over the water was great.- The pool / hot tub area is beautiful, and fairly large. I never felt like I was struggling to get a lounge chair. The hammocks are a nice touch.- The outdoor restaurant was pretty good. Nice location, good food.- The restaurants in the hotel are very good, especially the Strip House Steakhouse. It is very pricey (similar to New York City prices) but it is worth it. The food is excellent, the service is superb, and the overall atmosphere is great. We had a table overlooking the ocean which was a nice touch. If you want to spend $200 on a romantic dinner for two, I'd recommend the Strip House. The Italian restaurant on the mezzanine level is good too. We had breakfast and lunch there and the food is very good and reasonably priced.- The casino had $2 minimums for roulette... always a good thing.- The bar/lounge areas are lively, energetic, and fun.Negatives:- There are literally like 3 elevators in the entire hotel. We found ourselves waiting 5-10 minutes for a hotel at times. Not fun, especially being an impatient New Yorker.- There is minimal service at the Front Desk, which makes for long lines and more impatience on my part- Service overall was rude. The bellhop that greeted us and took our luggage to our room was very nice and very friendly. However, the employees working the front desk, casino and pool area are very rude.- Communication between the hotel and guests stinks... for example, we were looking for the Tony Roma restaurant in the hotel for about 15 minutes until we asked an employee and realized that it no longer existed. The same thing happened when we were looking to buy gelato. They have a big sign out near the pool area that says Gelato. When we went over to buy some, we could not find it. It was not until we asked an employee that we were told there was no gelato. Just overall disappointing...- The biggest disappointment of all was the beach area. I have been to some beautiful beaches in Puerto Rico, but this is not one of them. The beach is small, dirty, and the view is one that looks onto the nearby highway and construction sites. Not very relaxing at all, and VERY disappointing. I don't want to be sitting on a beach with a Corona and looking out onto a busy highway and construction site. Condado needs to do something to change the atmosphere there or just eliminate the beach all together. It was just plain ugly.- The casino was disappointing. Despite the low table minimums, the dealers were rude, and the games were questionable. While playing roulette, there were roughly TEN instances where the ball left the roulette wheel completely... and another 4 or 5 instances where the ball rolled along the edge of the numbers for 45 - 60 seconds before finally falling into a number. I've played roulette in many casinos and I've never seen the equipment THAT disfunctional or suspicious. The dealers didn't act like this was anything out of the ordinary. Either get some new equipment or get your staff to be a little more customer service oriented.Who wants to gamble when it seems like you're possibly being cheated out of a fair chance to win????? Not to suggest that the casino was rigging the games, because I am sure they were not... but when I left the casino after two hours I just had a bad taste in my mouth.Overall the Condado was a nice hotel with some good and some bad. Although I loved the room, the restaurants, and the pool area, I don't think I would stay there again unless there were some major upgrades to the hotel  staff.

I rolled my ankle on a small curb and fell. Now I have a large abraision on my leg as a souvenier. We rented a car from Dollar. It took us over an hour to pick up the car. In hindsight we would not rent a car again unless we plan to spend the majority of the trip outside of San Juan. Driving is a challenge in San Juan since the roads/highways are not clearly marked. We saw a lot more of the city than we planned to. We drove to El Yungue and enjoyed hiking some of the trails. We did get lost on the way but eventually found it. The weather was perfect and the people were very friendly. We would go back to PR to explore the rest of the island.

<Author>Eve76
<Content>Great hotel, great location My husband and I stayed four nights at the Condado Plaza, and we had a great time. The hotel is beautiful for a boutique hotel and nicely renovated. We felt very safe everywhere we went. It seems that the Police is stationed on every corner everywhere. Overall, we had a great stay.

<Author>whereswaugh
<Content>Stylish hotel/resort but a little far from everything The Condado Plaza Hotel is very stylish and the photos on Expedia and from reviewers on this site are for the most part accurate depictions of what you get. Our room was spacious and we had a view of the bay from a corner window. There is a bus stop outside the property but since we were there on a Sunday the hotel staff told us the schedule of buses was unpredictable. We could only find 2 restaurants outside of the hotel in walking distance - a Mexican restaurant and a Cuban/Puerto Rican restaurant that was only open for dinner. Food at both were OK and generally pricey for what we got. If there were other choices available outside of the hotel in walking distance the conceirge staff was unaware of them or unwilling to give us additional information.Concierge/Tour Booking - very disorganized!!! Different person with different information every time we went to the desk. We were first told that the tours they book are the same price as if we were to book directly on our own, but when we booked with another person we were charged a higher price. I don't mind that the hotel makes their commission for providing a booking service, but everyone working that desk should be able to explain that to customers. We had plenty of time to try and do it on our own had we known we were going to be charged a higher fee, but by the time the tour actually got booked it was too late for us to do any arrangements of our own.

<Author>love2traveltogether
<Content>Beautiful hotel, service, so-so... My husband and I recently returned from a 2 night stay at the Condado Plaza Hotel and Casino. We stayed at the hotel prior to our cruise. I have been going to Puerto Rico all of my life (37 years) and it is my favorite place in the world. We had visited San Juan last year and stayed at the Caribe Hilton. When we were visiting last year we went by the Condado Plaza Hotel and Casino and had seen all of the renovations. We knew we were going to come back in 2008 and noted it as a place to stay.  Upon our arrival we were met with a very long line for check in. There was actually only 1 person at the check in desk upon our arrival but slowly more people started to help out. We waited about 20 minutes and then we were assisted. We were told that the only ocean view rooms that were available had 2 Queen beds as opposed to the 1 King bed we had requested. We said it was o.k. and were given our key to room #842. The room was perfect. The renovations of both the lobby and the rooms are great. We had a great balcony with a perfect view of the ocean. The bathroom was really nice and everything was very clean. The beds were also very comfortable and after our first night we both noted what a great, restful sleep we had. We visited the casino and had a good time. Ate breakfast both mornings at the Gusto D'Italia Restaurant. The food was very good and plentiful, the service not so great. The waiter was not overly friendly and we had to ask for things more than once. We had ice cream in the Gusto D'Italia one night and the ice cream attendant was very nice. The bar was also very nice and they make a great Pina Colada. The beach area is very small and was quite shaded so we opted to sit by the rock wall on the side of the hotel. It was extremely peaceful and the sound of the waves was wonderful. The elevators, I have to say, were very quick. I had read on several reviews about how slow they were but we did not find this to be a problem. Our biggest complaint was when we called down to the desk and asked for 2 more towels and 2 wash cloths as they had not been replenished by the room attendant the day before. What they brought us was 1 towel and when my husband explained that we needed 1 more towel and 2 wash cloths was told they would be coming right away. After an hour had passed, and they still had not arrived, my husband called the front desk and was told that they are very busy and were not sure when they could get them to us. This for us was a big turn off as a hotel of this caliber should have stocked the towels in the room to begin with and then they should have definitely brought us what we requested but then to be told they are too busy, that was not right. Fortunately this was our only complaint and hope to visit the Condado Plaza Hotel and Casino again in the very near future. All in all, we would highly recommend a stay at the Condado Plaza Hotel and Casino.

<Author>KipNYC
<Content>Magnificent Property Marred by Terrible Service Every physical aspect of the Condado is visually fresh and aesthetically pleasing. The lobby, room (city view), pool area and even casino are all a joy. The cubicle shower is a curious (i.e., fun) experience (door leaks a bit though). Balconies are always nice. The three pools (fresh water, salt water, hot tub) are all in great shape, and who isn't tempted by the swim-up bar? No-password wi-fi not only in the rooms but throughout the property.Unfortunately, the act of actually staying at the resort becomes a task rather than an experience. Here's the rundown:--For most of my stay only one of the three elevators was operating (this is the second hotel in a row where I've seen this -- trying to cut electricity costs?). A ten-story property cannot have only one working elevator; it's simply not an option.--The tour desk is an absolute disaster. They only book their own tours (the Condado is part of a local chain). My tour for the first day was rained out, and the lady who tried to reschedule couldn't confirm what was being offered when and assured me that someone would get back to me by 9PM (for a tour at 8AM the next morning). Sure enough, the next morning nobody knew anything about anything. Bottom line: In three full days they couldn't schedule a single tour for me. If you can make alternative arrangements (Gray Line, etc.) do so.--My last full day I returned to my room about 1PM after swimming. There was only one housekeeper on the entire floor, and she was sitting in a room watching television! I came back at 4:40PM and my room STILL wasn't made. I had stuff to do and told them not to bother.--Ordered a Heineken at the pool, and then watched for ten minutes while the waitress chit-chatted with the bartender. Got up and left.--Had a casino dealer more interested in the baseball game on the screen rather than actually dealing. Very annoying. (On a side note, a lot of local trash gamble in the Condado's casino. Don't expect a Vegas business convention atmosphere.) My guess is that the bigger chains skim off the best staff and the Condado has to settle for second-tier employees. Bottom Line: If you're a low-maintenance, laid-back sort of traveler (and this is a beach resort, after all), then the Condado will probably do you just fine. But if good service is an important part of your vacation experience, then be sure to explore other options.One last point: Be sure to book directly through the hotel (their website is easy to Google). They have several packages that might not show up on Expedia or Travelocity. In my case it was the Fourth Night Free deal.

<Content>Not what I expected,would not stay here again I do not usually take the time nor feel compelled to write a review after a stay at a hotel but this time I do. This was my second time to visit Puerto Rico and I felt I had done my research about which hotels we might want to stay in as we wanted to stay in the Metro area. I had read a lot of the reviews on the Condado Hotel and felt there were more good ones than bad. I should have paid more attention to the bad ones. At least they fit our experience more than the good ones. We arrived on Sunday around 10:30 p.m. and I expected check in to go quickly as we had reservations and it was late in the evening. The hotel lobby looked as it had online in the photos.We had reserved a room with a private balcony overlooking the Atlantic with a king size bed. The room we were assigned had two double beds. So, down the slow elevators and back to the front desk where we had to wait to have this corrected. There were three people working the front desk, two of them were busy and the third one was staring at a computer screen and never looked up or asked us or anyone else if we needed help. So, we waited for the person that had originally helped us. The room assignment was corrected and we went back up to the new room. It was correct this time. The room also appeared as it had online but was not as clean as I had expected. The shower in the bathroom had mildew on the ceiling and the floor did not look vacuumed. The room also had a musty smell. There does not appear to be a ventilation fan in the bathroom. There was moisture on the window looking out to the balcony because of the humidity and you could see where some previous occupant of the room had written [--] You. You would think housekeeping could wipe the outside of the window between room occupants. The room seemed to be cleaned better after the first night. Note to traveler: make sure you put the 鈥淐lean This Room鈥?sign on your door when you leave your room in the morning. The other thing with housekeeping, which seemed to be the only friendly staff, was that they only put one wash cloth in the room everyday. There were two of us staying in the room and everyday I had to ask for another wash cloth. Back to the first 5 minutes in the room. We proceeded to get settled in the room and the power went out in the hotel. We were now standing in a dark room with just the glow through the window illuminating the room. I don鈥檛 really blame this on the hotel but it was one of the first of many annoying things to come. After about 15 minutes of on again off again episodes and one scary moment of being stuck in the elevator for a brief moment power was restored.The pool area is ok but I have been to several that make this really rank. The pool is opened 24 hours but make sure you bring a towel from the room if you go down in the evenings or you will not have a towel They say they provide towels at the pool but the towel shack closes around 6:00 p.m. One night I had gone down to use the hot tub and lay by the pool and enjoy the moonlight and the sounds of the ocean and felt stalked by a security guard which kept looking and walking around me as if I didn鈥檛 belong there. I almost confronted him and asked him to stop but decided to let it go. If you are going to have drinks at the pool bar be prepared to pay around $20 for two basic cocktails. Note to traveler: go to the store down the block and buy some rum, a bottle of coke and some plastic glasses and take your drink to the pool. Not one time did a waitress or waiter come over to ask if we needed a drink or anything. Another afternoon we had walked out to the pool area, set our things down and proceeded to the lagoon (beach) area to put our feet in the water and on the way back in we were stopped and asked to see the key card to our room to prove that we were hotel guest while other people just filed on by. I鈥檓 glad I had it in my swim suit pocket! I am 51 years old, clean cut and well dressed and had just walked out to the pool area from the hotel 5 minutes prior to this and he didn鈥檛 say 鈥淚鈥檓 sorry鈥?or explain why he was asking. Yes, I was insulted!!! After that we really didn鈥檛 make use of the pool area.If you want to go to the beach go to Escambron, down the road towards Old San Juan, or Carolina beach in Isla Verde. Both are part of the Blue Flag program. If you go to El Yungue stop by Luquillo beach on your way back.We rented a car from Budget which is in the tower across the street also part of the Condado Hotel. The Budget Rental people were great. We got the car we wanted and quickly. We were able to return it at the airport which is what we wanted to do. Note to traveler: if you rent a car be prepared for the parking situation at the Condado. You have to take a ticket out of the machine to get in the parking garage, pray you can find a parking spot and then when you are ready to go out again you have to take it to the valet desk which is located outside in front of the hotel, write your room number, your name and sign it, hand it to a valet and get it validated and then go get your car out of the garage. You must do this every time you come and go which is very annoying! They do not explain this system well and sometimes it went smoothly and other times the person behind the parking desk acted like they didn鈥檛 know what was going on and would tell you something completely different from what you had been doing. They tell you that in the end you will be charged a flat rate of $15.00 a day but this system does not instill confidence. We saw several people as confused as we were with the whole parking process. Also, just because you are a hotel guest does not mean you are guaranteed a parking space. There is an area designated for hotel guest but no one monitors who parks in these spots. If you come and go 3 to 4 times a day there are times you will return to the garage to see the 鈥淕arage Full鈥?sign and have no option but to park down the street in a public lot or valet park at the hotel. We had no option but to valet park one time and when we came to get the car they didn鈥檛 know where it was at first. Plus the valet parking rate is much more expensive. Note to traveler: if you have been out to a beach other than the one at the hotel there is no alternate elevator to your room you will have to go through the lobby. During the week with business men, etc. this can seem uncomfortable.We did not spend any time in the Casino as that is not our thing and we did not eat at the Strip House as we have one where we live. We did eat at the Italian restaurant which was not good. If you like Italian food don鈥檛 get it here. You also can get breakfast in this same space in the morning and we ate breakfast twice and it was fine. If you like coffee, request the Puerto Rican coffee otherwise they bring regular coffee.We did try the bar but after no wait person came to take our order we went up to the bar to order and the bartender just continued to talk to someone and ignored us even after saying 鈥渃an we get a drink?鈥?We gave up at that point.Another annoying thing at this hotel is the doors to the rooms. It is impossible to close them without a loud slam and I mean loud. So, early mornings and late evenings you are aware of the comings and goings of other guests while you are sleeping or relaxing in your own room.In general, I felt the staff was rude and unaccommodating. I think this is more of a business and convention hotel than a vacationing one. Based on our experience I was expecting check out to be an unpleasant experience and to our surprise it wasn鈥檛. They even started to say 鈥渢hank you鈥? I know we were staying at this hotel during the 鈥渙ff season鈥?but service is service. I feel if we had stayed somewhere else we might have had a great vacation. I would not stay here again. Next time we will stay at one of the Isla Verde hotels or one of the resort hotels.

<Author>Mamagata
<Content>Lovely hotel This was the second time we stayed at the Condado Plaza. We were there 2 1/2 years ago and preferred it then to its new, modern look, but there's no going back. Surprisingly, it's a very popular place. Forget Chili's across the street. It's very noisy, crowded, and pedestrian, Ajili Mojili is good if you like Puerto Rican food.

<Author>bdbmommy
<Content>Great stay despite some snafu's We just returned from a wonderful vacation and our first time in Puerto Rico. After initially booking at the Gran Melia in PR I read some negative reviews on tripadvisor and switched to the Condado Plaza. I can't emphasize how happy I am that I did. We arrived on Monday morning and checked right in without a wait. There was a problem with the first room we were given. The sliding door to the balcony had been left open and the bathroom was infested with mosquitos. Once we brought this to managements attention we were immdiately given another comparable room without hesitation. Every staff member we encountered throughout our stay was effiicient, friendly and polite. The head of guest relations Henry Neuman was very present and approachable. Javier was my favorite porter at the door. Any negative seeming issues we had were quickly dealt with including a leak in our room on our last night there. I also had a mishap with a dryer in the small laundry room on the premises that ate my quarters. It was so nice to be able to wash my clothes and not pack up a suitcase full of sand that a dryer that ate my quarters was a small price to pay for the convenience of not having to go off the grounds to do laundry.I would echo other reviewers sentiments that the food by the pool was very pricey and of mediocre quality. After one lunch there (we were too tired upon arrival to go forraging outside the hotel for a meal) we did not eat at the hotel at all. Having a Starbucks on the grounds helped get the day started with ease and we ate off the grounds for the rest of the day during our stay. During the week the action at the pool was manageable and it was not difficult to find an empty chair. Our ten year old son had a blast on the water slide and made friends while waiting on line. We had Diana as our server for poolside drinks and she was lovely and available without being overbearing. Like other reviewers I observed that there were people at the pool who did not seem to be guests of the hotel. When entire families show up at a resort pool in street clothing it does seem a bit suspect and I saw that more than once during the week. However once the weekend hit and the hotel was at what seemed to be capacity they began issuing wrist bands with the towels. The lagoon beach is small but had some fun snorkeling. We saw squid, octopus, puffer fish, trumpet fish and numerous other colorful tropical fish.I would suggest if you like to snorkel bring your own gear. This is a resort and they charge resort prices for gear rental.Yes, as mentioned in other reviews the elevators are slow. It seems as though there just aren't enough elevators for the amount of people the hotel can hold. During the week it really wasn't a problem but when the hotel filled up on the weekend with conventions and weddings it became more noticeable. Most people just took it in stride. The rooms were kept very clean. I would call the decor tropical West Elm. My one complaint about the rooms would be that the walls were a bit on the thin side. We got around mostly by cab after one attempt to go local and take the bus that resulted in a wait that was over an hour. If you like surfer communities go to Ocean Park beach and go to Pinky's or Top Hamburger for lunch. Everywhere we went in Puerto Rico the service was friendly and a refreshing change of pace.The absolute highlight of our vacation was the restaurant Marmalade in Old San Juan. Due to my line of work I have eaten food prepared by all the best chefs in the country including Batali, Flay, Morimoto, et al. and the food and service at Marmalade was by far the best I have ever experienced. They were completely unfazed by our bringing a ten year old in with us and did everything they could to accomodate his picky habits and make us comfortable. The whole experience was so outstanding we went back a second night without him. If you go to Marmalade ask to sit in Bernice's section. She undertands the concept of sublime service.All in all a wonderful vacation and I absolutely would not hesitate to go back!

<Author>USFGIRL
<Content>This hotel definitely exceeded my expectations If you are thinking about staying in Condado, I recommend the Condado Plaza Hotel. Recently renovated, (although the painting on one side of the building was not finished) the hotel has a contemporary feel and look to it from the lobby to the room itself. A huge aquarium greets you as you walk in and the rest of the lobby and mezzanine level, where the casino is, are decorated with an art deco style that screams fun. The room was the highlight however. The new, plush furniture and plasma tv were a perfect fit with the bright colors of the walls and area rug. The room was tiled throughout which gave it a nice, clean look. I never want to stay in a carpeted hotel room again! The stand alone shower with glass walls in the spacious bathroom was a big hit with the gf and just added to the uniqueness of the entire room. The digital thermostat was a nice thing to have as well. For the small amount of time spent in the room, we really enjoyed coming back to it after a long day. Our friends who stayed at the Hilton next door said our room blew theirs away! The ocean views from our room were breathtaking. The grounds were well manicured with hammocks and lounge chairs within a stone's throw of the Atlantic for those who prefer peace and quiet while the 2 pools (one with a swim up bar and huge slide) were perfect for enjoying a cocktail or two and/or letting the kids burn off some energy. The staff was friendly and knowlegable and all spoke English. The only complaints I had were the bathroom sink drained very slowly and was not fixed even after notifying the front desk. The elevators were extremely slow which caused most elevator rides to be crammed with guests as it seemed people were constantly waiting to ride. Finally, the room service prices were too expensive in my opinion...$6 for corn flakes is a bit much. Overall, for the money spent on the room, I think we lucked out and would recommend this hotel to anyone.

There was almost no carpeting on the floor, which was great. The pool area was wonderful with fresh water pool, salt water pool, and hot tub. There is also a pool in the laguna tower. The bar at the pool was great, but very expensive ($10 per drink). They also had nice music and live band on Saturday. We never ate at the hotel restaurants. We tried to have breakfast at the Italian restaurant on our last day, but we left the place when nobody took our order or offered us anything to drink after sitting there with the menus for 15 minutes, despite the fact that they had 5 waiters for 5 tables. <Content>Absolutely Fantastic The Condado Plaza Hotel and Casino is an absolutely fantastic place! It's hip, funky, and stylish with also a very practical twist. <Author>hammyryder79
<Content>Slick, stylish and efficient My husband and I spent 5 nights at the Condado Plaza for our honeymoon and were really pleased. It may not be an obvious 'romantic' choice for a honeymoon but we'd been recommended it by 2 sets of friends for its good value, location, efficiency etc... and I dont believe we could have chosen better anywhere else in San Juan (maybe the Ritz Carlton but, 5 times the price!)Firstly arrived on a 9am flight, check in was not until 4pm but as I had previously enquired about an early check in our room was available straight away. Secondly we were upgraded for free to a gorgeous ocean view room so we were doubly pleased straight away! The room was great - slick, modern, spacious, loads of room in the bathroom and lovely comfy bed and lounge area. The hotel is in the final stages of renovation but at no point did this interfere with our stay. All the staff were friendly and efficient. The reception staff quick, helpful and we even witnessed them deal with a lost child in a lovely manner. The bar/restaurant staff at the Aqua pool bar were friendly as were the concierge, travel desk and bell boys. We never had to wait more than 2 minutes for a taxi which were hailed from over the road.We ate at Aqua bar for lunch (very nice salads) and had a meal in the Strip House which was superb - sultry burlesque decor and fabulous steaks. There is a wine waiter too who was very knowledgable and not at all patronising like some i've experienced.The casino is average - they dont have a texas hold 'em table so we went to the Marriott one night to play there. They have roulette and black jack though.The hotel is only about 5-10 mins in a taxi to Old San Juan traffic pending ($12) so not far at all. Old San Juan was beautiful with its cobbled streets and colourful shop fronts but I actually quite like the fact we could 'escape' from the hussle and bussle. Within walking distance from the hotel are numerous restaurants and designer shops (Gucci, Salvatore Feragamo, Dior, Louis Vuitton, Mont Blanc etc...) and boutiques.I would definately stay at this hotel if I were to go back and would recommended to all demographs.

<Author>drewcorey
<Content>Great Value..Enjoyed Stay First of all let me preface this by saying you can put 10 people in a room and get 10 different opinions. We recently stayed at the Condado Plaza and have to say we were very satisfied with the overall property based upon our daily room rate. We stayed when they were running a special of stay 3 nights and get the 4th free. So, the average room rate came out to be around $150.00 per night. I see a lot of people complaining about additional charges beyond the room rate. These are statutory charges that are imposed by Puerto Rico....so it dosen't matter where you stay you are paying the charges. Some hotels might include these in the rate so you have to inquire prior to booking. The staff was very courteous and friendly and seemed to want to help whenever they could. The property and the rooms where clean and recently renovated. You read all these reviews about people who are complaining about the property. Well realize your not staying at the El San Juan Hotel, Intercontintenal, etc...where you are paying $350.-500. per night. And to be honest with you I don't know how much better they would have been. The hotel is located in an accessible part of town where you are not locked into eating at the hotel. There a places within walking distance from the hotel. A great place we ate at was Ropa Vieja. We also got upgraded to an ocean view for no charge that was absolutely beautiful. The previous review complained about the ocean being closed. We were there at the same time and the the surf was extremely dangerous and you wouldn't have wanted to go near the water. Is it the hotels fault? Casino is small but more than adequate. Pool was very nice...fresh and saltwater...swim up bar....small public beach in a bay area not right on the ocean. The view from the room was breathtaking and the sounds of the crashing waves against the sea wall were so soothing. <Author>BXTRAVELER1
<Content>Mixed Thoughts When I arrived at the Condado, I was initially very excited as I pulled up in my rental car. From the outside, I felt like I was going to be staying at a top notch hotel with impecable service. While my overall stay was pleasant, I had mixed feelings about the hotel. PROS: It is definitely in the best location. Situated at the end of the Condado strip within walking distance of shopping, cafes, rest. and other hotels while just steps from the bridge to old san juan where you can find the best nightlife in the carribean. The pool area is very relaxing. You have many options. You can sit in a shaded area on a lounge chair along the larger pool, or roast in the sun by the smaller pool. Or, for a perfect, relaxing nap you can chill on one of the hammocks strung between palm trees on the main lawn overlooking the ocean. The overall atmosphere down by the pool is amazing and sure to wipe away any stress you came down with. What makes it even better is the outstanding pool staff of waitresses and bartenders. They were so friendly, fast and personable that I was compelled to leave a very generous tip. However, the pricing of the food made me choke!!! $13.00 for a turkey wrap..Even in NY we do not have prices like that. The cleaning staff do a great job as well and are friendly. CONS: As great as the hotel appears to look from the outside, I could not believe how they overlook small details that really ruined my initial impression of the hotel. For example, the window in my room was so filthy and dingy that I could barely get a clear view. My room also had many marks and scrapes on the walls. I also noticed paint peeling from the outside of the hotel near the balconies. For a hotel that just underwent major renovations, I don't see how they can allow these very visable eyesores to exist; especially since it would not take much effort to fix. That makes me wonder how much they do care about customer service and appearance. If they want to classify themselves as a luxury hotel, you cannot have these conditions. Also, when I checked in, I had to wait for 10 min. while the clerk was on the phone. And, he was not friendly at all. When I asked him about late check out, he gave me an attitude. Not the right thing to do to a first time guest. I was also a little dispointed with the beach. Having paid the $$, I would expect to have a little more privacy on the beach. They seem to allow all the locals to use the beach which got very crowded and noisy. If I wanted to go to a public beach, I could have stayed at a much cheaper hotel in downtown San Juan and walked to a beach. Overall, I did enjoy my stay. But as a frequent carribean traveler, you get more critical of the little details that make a big difference. With the exception of my check in clerk, the staff was very professional and accomodating. I did get the late check out without much resistance and the girl who checked me out explained the bill in great detail and even found a mistake from the parking garage...THANK YOU!!! I would stay here again just because of the location of the hotel and the outstanding pool and lounge area. But please, rethink about allowing the beach to be open to the public and take care of those little eyesores. They can really bring the appearance down and make the hotel look sloppy and dirty. I will be back!!

<Author>FL_foodie
<Content>Outstanding Service, Beautifully Renovated Hotel My husband and I just got back from a few days at the Condado Plaza, and we had a wonderful time. The place is beautiful - well designed and decorated, and absolutely spotless throughout. The new lobby is now open, and we never had to wait more than a minute for an elevator.I can't say enough about the service at this hotel. As should be obvious from all of Henry's responses on this site, the staff really wants to do everything they can to make your stay wonderful. My husband was attending a conference and had to arrange a couple of business lunches. Everyone in the restaurant bent over backwards to ensure that they had everything they needed without being intrusive. They made my husband look like quite the captain of industry!The location of the hotel is good, within walking distance to a few restaurants and a short cab ride to Isla Verde and Old San Juan. There were always plenty of cabs lined up in front of the property. We ended up eating at the Italian restaurant at the hotel one night because we were exhausted from sightseeing, and the food and service were excellent. This hotel has the best margaritas I've had anywhere. Travelers should be aware, though, that this is not the best place to go if they're looking for a great beach. The hotel is on the ocean, but most of the shore is rocky, not sand. There is a small beach on a protected cove, so there are no waves. The locals seemed to bring their small children there, so it was fairly crowded for such a small beach. The pools, on the other hand, were beautiful and uncrowded.We had an oceanfront room. It was fairly large, and had a great view and a completely private balcony. The bathroom was enormous. However, as others have observed, the sliding frosted glass doors to the bathroom did not provide a great deal of privacy. There was also a fair amount of noise from the hallway and from the room adjoining ours. Neither was a problem for us at night, but if you had obnoxious neighbors I could see this being an issue.Overall, this is a great place for business travelers or those looking for a central location from which to explore the island. It is not the place for those looking for long walks on the beach or swims in the ocean.

<Author>olde_tyme_style
<Content>Lively fun on the strip I actually stayed at this property almost 4 years ago. I had stayed once before in 2002. The hotel and central location to surrounding areas was so great that I decided to return. The room had water views of the bay and the ocean as well as the hotel strip and was in a high rise tower with a balcony. The room was clean, comfortable and the bathroom was nicely done.The hotel is beachfront with lounge chairs on the ocean side and has a salt water pool and freshwater pool on the ocean side. The pools were well kept, but a little crowded with guests. Nothing bad though. There are many lounge chairs near the pool and on the ocean side of the property as well as scattered hammocks to catch the ocean breeze. There are also some nice hidden places to take tropical background pictures. On the bay side there is a great pool. Not many guests realize this pool is there and therefore, it is not crowded no matter when you take a dip. The poolside also has lounge chairs and is uncrowded. There is also a nice jacuzzi near this pool. You will most likely have it to yourself. At night you can sit in the jacuzzi and listen to the coquis in the background. There is also a watersports pavilion (I think it's privately owned) at the bayside if you walk down the drive along side of the hotel. I rented a kayak. The employee took my room number to charge the rental to my room but the best part was I was never charged. I also noticed other non-motorized rentals, I particularly remember aqua cycles. You get to use the entire bay and even toward the ocean, if you dare.The casino is large and fun and is always happening at night. There are a lot of games to choose from and many people playing, creating a nice atmosphere. The hotel has various on site restaurants. The buffet was my favorite for breakfast. There was hot and cold varieties. Try it at least once. There is an amazing ocean view through the wall of windows. The ocean spray even sometimes hits the window. The location can't be beaten. Steps from the main hotel is the bus into Old San Juan. It stops running about 10 or 11, but a cab ride back later is reasonable. The hotel is also on the Condado hotel strip - great for food, fun, shopping, casino hopping, bars. There is even a small public beach on the ocean side if you walk down a ways. The conciege can set you up with fun excursions to explore the rainforest or a nighttime kayaking expedition (transportation provided) from the ocean in Farjado through a channel into a bioluminescent bay. It was such a unique experience I will never forget (wear a bathing suit, you can hop in for a swim and watch the water light up flurescent blue as you move)I would certainly return in the future if I had the opportunity.

<Content>Perhaps When They Are Finally Finished . . . The company I work for sends its top reps on a trip with a guest annually. This year they chose Puerto Rico as the destination and after much research chose the Condado Plaza Hotel and Casino. Over 400 employees and guests stayed between December 6th - December 11th and unfortunately while I can't speak for all of us I know that my husband and I as well as many of the others we talked to were sadly disappointed.Previous reviews were responded to with the note that the lobby would be finished on 12/3. This was not the case. When we arrived on 12/6 the lobby had minimal furniture (more was added during our stay) and they were still working on it when we left 12/11. There was no check in desk on the beach side but a table had been set up where attendees received their packet from my employer. We were then directed to stand online where a gentleman working from a laptop computer was assigning rooms. We had been told check in would begin at 3 PM so when we arrived at 2:30 we were not alarmed that the room was not ready but as time wore on our frustrations grew. A colleague and her husband waited with us as the room they had finally been assigned to had other guests already in it. At 5:30 after the coordinator of the event found out we had been waiting 3 hours for a room, miraculously a room was made available with a king size bed and an ocean view. We mentioned our disappointment to our coordinator as the group was leaving in 30 minutes for a welcome dinner and we had to still get our luggage up to the room, shower and change. The hotel organized a Town Car to pick us up and get us to the dinner. When we returned to our room that evening a fruit and cheese platter as well as a bottle of wine was waiting for us. I was pleased that the hotel had made an effort to acknowledge our frustration but it was obvious that the cheese had been siting out for some time and was probably left out for us soon after we departed. I know that the staff would have no idea what time we would be returning (although there were buses scheduled to take everyone back which were organized by our tour group that worked closely with the hotel) but perhaps it would have been better to put the cheese and fruit into the refrigerator with a note next to the bottle of wine on the desk . . . We soon learned that check in frustrations were not limited to the first day. While less than 100 people arrived on day one, the others (over 300 people) arrived the next day. The same lonely check in table remained. I heard from others that our 3 hour wait was short in comparison . . . Many people waited 7+ hours to be assigned a room. Each time a room assignment was given a staff member had to run across the skyway (located a floor above us) to program the room keys. We also heard stories of the luggage guests had checked upon their arrival while waiting for their room went AWOL which added further delays.I understand that the official grand opening is to take place on either 12/31 or 1/1 . . . Perhaps by then all of the amenities mentioned in the book located in our room will be up and running. They have Tony Roma's listed as a restaurant option and there is a sign for it in the Laguna Tower also know as the building with the Bay views near the elevators but I was told it was closed during renovations. We were unable to eat in the Strip House but if it is anything like the one we have here in NYC while it is very expensive the food is extraordinary. The only real dining option is an Italian family style restaurant that charges $9.95 for scrambled eggs with sausage, some toast and I will say the two largest hash browns I have ever seen. We learned right before we left that this establishment is not associated with the hotel so any gratuities charged to your room bill are given to the wait staff two weeks later and a large portion is taken out by the owners to defray the paperwork costs associated with getting the funds from the hotel. While the food is not bad I would not say it is great but unless you go down the street to Chilli's or one of the very overpriced local places on Ashford Avenue ($13.95 for an Italian sub) then your only other option is a 24 hour Subway down the street or the Starbucks immediately adjacent to the hotel. You can't even get a soda or a bottle of water in the hotel as there are no machines. You can take a nice walk or a cab ride to a local 24 hour Walgreens and purchase items there and place them in the room fridge. The hotel gift shop where at least per the sign in the bathroom is where you can purchase the Clear line of toiletries (vegan) they make available to guests is not currently open. The brunch the hotel served participants on our last day of meetings was quite lovely and even included an omelet station. We personally had no problems with our room once we got there. It was beautiful with a flat screen TV and easily accessible free high speed Internet access. We had a beautiful view overlooking the ocean and it was only on the last day when a tropical storm came through the area that it turned into a swimming pool of sorts because there was nowhere for the rain water to go. Rain water seems to be an issue in several places at this property . . . Another party in our group let me know they had leaking issues in one of their two adjoining rooms and housekeeping did not want to keep bringing towels. They also had a problem with one of the showers and had to use the one that was working in the other room the rest of their party was staying in. I noticed a towel in the lobby area by a window soaking up rain that was coming inside and in the walkway from the two buildings they had plastic garbage pails just like the ones in our hotel room strategically placed in a row to catch the rain that was making its way inside. They must have missed a few spots because I did feel an occasional drop hit me as I made my way across.The best part of our stay was the staff -- especially those working the front doors on the beach side. They offered a truly first class experience one would expect from such an establishment. Doors to cars were opened as passengers entered and exited vehicles, taxi's were quickly dispatched from across the street on the Bay side, doors to the building were opened for guests as they entered and exited the building and perhaps most importantly service was always offered with a smile, kindness and assistance whenever needed.We did not spend our time at the beach but I did read in an older tour guide book that the beach at this hotel is one of the better ones in the Condado area because of the reef creating a natural barrier for the waves. On our last night we did check out the indoor whirlpool located on the Bay side next to the gym. While small, the water was lovely but alas the jets were not working. Engineering was called but did not arrive before we left. My husband and I did not spend much time in the small casino but it seemed nice enough. We did use the ATM located in the gaming area as the one in the lobby was out of order during our stay and we were pleased to see that there was no service charge for using the machine.I believe that once everything is finally in place that this property has wonderful possibilities but alas despite their attempts to complete everything by December 3rd there is still work to be done.

<Author>tee-em
<Content>Fantastic We have stayed in a number of hotels in the world and the Condado Plaza has the most unique rooms we have seen. Don't let the exterior of the hotel fool you. Guest check-in is on the second floor Mezzanine level and connects by overland bridge to the casino and rest of the hotel. Major renovations are still being done on the Mezzanine floor but there is a great Italian Restaurant on that level. We arrived late and they were happy to serve us at 12:00 midnight (It is open till 1:00 am on weekends although the guest services book says it closes at midnight.We had been upgraded by Mr. Neuman to an ocean view room and it was beautiful. The view to the ocean and to old San Juan from not only the balcony but also the windows on two sides of the room is spectacular. You can't beat the sound of the waves on the beach immediately underneath your room.The rooms themselves are brightly decorated in a contemporary style with a very comfortable pillow top king bed, an ultra modern L shaped couch, marble working table, and flat screen tv. The bathroom is huge with a completely glassed in shower and double sliding glass and wood doors.Contrary to what I had read in previous (all older) reviews, the staff we very professional and friendly. We would like to specifically thank Mr. Neuman for his speedy personal response to all the questions and concerns we had before booking. No canned response here like in many of the large chains (if you can even find someone to contact). He had advised us that the hotel had undertaken major initiates in staff training and it shows.We can hardly wait until the renovations are totally finished so we can return to this beautiful property.

<Author>lujain
<Content>Good location and service, noisy construction mess My husband and I stayed at the Condado Plaza for 6 nights in late September 2007. We were in a lagoon view room in the lagoon tower.The hotel offers easy access to Old San Juan. There is only a small beach near the hotel. There is a lot of construction going on in that area, both inside the hotel and outside as well. The rooms have been completed, but they are still working on the lobby in the ocean tower. The construction area (the lobby, the walkway to the casino, and the casino) was a mess. Also, there was a jackhammer drilling in the casino during working hours. The room was nicely decorated with green and blue hues. The view of the lagoon was gorgeous. The bed was comfortable, and there was a flat screen HDTV. My husband complained that the TV was not set up properly (something about people's faces being improperly squished), and the content was not in HD. My husband says there was no way to adjust the aspect ratio on the TV (whatever that means). The glass shower in the bathroom leaked. Also, the sliding door to the bathroom did not offer a lot of privacy.The 2 guest elevators in the lagoon tower were down about half of the time. We used the service elevator at those times. Dining options in the hotel are limited. We tried Tony Roma's, where the food was sub-par. We ate breakfast at the Italian restaurant. My vegie omelette had an entire bell pepper chopped into it. The pancakes were gigantic and heavy, not light and fluffy. The fruit cup included canned fruit. We had better luck with more basic items, like oatmeal, poached eggs, and toast. We had room service a few times. Service was good and the chocolate cake was yummy.We took full advantage of a $300 resort credit offered by the hotel. We used it for parking for our rental car, dining, and in-room movies. There is a large selection of in-room movies.The hotel offers some nice touches, like fresh flowers in the common areas. The renovated gym looked pretty nice. However, I would not recommend staying at this hotel until the construction is completed (supposedly in late November 2007). With the unsightly mess and the noise, the hotel does not offer a restful, peaceful environment that I would want on a vacation. I would probably go with the Caribe Hilton or the Marriott instead.

Again, we liked it but they desperately need to oil the sliding doors - you could wake the dead opening them.Great location - Starbucks across the street - restaurants in walking distance, nice beach at the hotel and a 10 min ride (tops) to Old San Juan, 45 min to the rainforest.So, we loved it - it was a great time and we would definitely recommend it. Hope to go back next year - apparently May - Nov is 'off season' and barring any hurricanes it's a great time to be there.

<Author>terps94
<Content>Great time at Condado Plaza We had a 7 night stay at the Condado Plaza for our 10th anniversary in August 2007. After a lot of research, I chose the hotel based on location and price. I knew it was undergoing renovations (as is every hotel in the Caribbean in the summer off-season) but I e-mailed the hotel management before our visit and was assured that the renovations wouldn't affect our stay. We had to ask for help locating the check-in desk because it was not right where you enter the building, but up one level. Check in was quick and easy. We had booked a city vista room, but received a complimentary upgrade to an ocean vista room in the Ocean Tower. The room was great - the view, the decor, the bathroom, all of it. It was unlike any typical Marriott, Hilton, Holiday Inn, etc. but really unique. To get to our room, we came in through the Laguna Tower, walked up the one flight of stairs (never even thought about using the elevator that others have commented on for one flight), walked across the tunnel between the two buildings, and took the elevator up. Both elevators and the pool elevator in the Ocean Tower were always working and there was never a delay of any kind.We went in the casino once for about 20 minutes. It was busy at times, but never packed, and it looked like it could easily accomodate the guests. The pools were beautiful and scenic. Again, they were never really packed and there were never any problems getting a chair or anything. The bar at the pool was nice. The beach is small and also public, as is every beach in San Juan - even the Marriott and such have to let the public on, we learned. However, the staff would bring chairs for you if you wanted and the beach was plenty big enough for the people using it. The water was clear, calm, and warm.Having a taxi stand at the hotel was convenient for getting around. Prices are set so you know you're not getting scammed. The bus stop is also right at the hotel and easy to get into Old San Juan for 75 cents. There are lots of good Puerto Rican and other restaurants within a 5-10 block walk down Ashford Avenue. It was a nice stroll in the evening to find a restaurant if we weren't in Old San Juan. We never ate at the restaurants in the hotel because we'd rather experience the local flavors. Overall, our experience with the hotel, the staff, and the amenities was great. When the renovations are complete, it will be even nicer, but we had no complaints. Mr. Neumann and his staff (especially Jean Pierre, who went out of his way to find a tour for us when the one we signed up for wound up being full) were wonderful and we would recommend the Condado Plaza to others.

<Content>False advertising and lies!!! But good location and nice rooms. This was our first time visiting San Juan, Puerto Rico. Booked our room online via their website and called the hotel 4-5 times personally to ask specific questions about our reservations and ammenities of the hotel. The people who answered the calls were very nice and promised we get the type of room we asked for (two double beds non-smoking). Their website talks about a cafe and lounge. Not once did the staff let us know that there cafe was CLOSED due to renovations and that there was NO lounge, live music, or club in the hotel. We opted to stay here due to the special promotion they had via their website which saved us a couple hundred bucks. After a very long flight over to San Juan and upon arriving to the hotel we found ourselves at what was the temporary check-in area. Only one person at the desk and upon checking in the guy told us that there were no rooms available that we reserved and that we would have to take a single king bed with an inflatable bed instead for the night. That was not satisfactory to us so we demanded something better. He went to the back and suddenly a room with a double bed became available. There was no apology and he said that reservations are only a preference and not gauranteed!!! They had only one elevator working the whole time. The other one was out of order. I do not understand why they did not fix this problem. The wait was long for the elevator and it got very crammed. The hotel staff also used this very same elevator as well which explains why it would get very crammed. The elevator problem should have been a top priority to fix asap. We were giving a room with the view of the lagoon which was very nice. Nicely renovated room. Comfy beds and pillows. The ac worked nicely but had trouble trying to fix the temp on the panel that got stuck. The bathroom had very nice fixtures and the shower worked great. The cleaning people were always very nice. We wanted to watch a movie. Called downstairs and they informed us that our tv was not hooked up to be able to watch the movie of our choice. It was a bummer. We ordered room service once and it was a super rip off, outrageous! The girl who took our order was very rude and to top it off our bill came out to around $70 for three people!!! Upon asking for an explanation it was simply said that the price is what the computer makes it to come out to. That was the last and only time we ordered room service.The Italian restaurant had the nicest staff. Very friendly and very helpful. Tony Roma's was just alright. Jose was the best server there. He gave us tips about the town and it helped a ton. Long wait for food there too and they told us that they were out of hamburger buns for our orders. Starbucks across the ways was perfect for our breakfast needs. Even saw a famous Spanish soap opera actor in there! The location of the hotel is right in the middle. We hopped onto the bus to catch a ride to Old San Juan (only cost 75 cents each way) and the bus stop was right in front of the hotel. Also got onto the same bus to get to Plaza Las Americas, the gigantic mall in Hato Rey. Saved a lot of money that way than taking a cab everywhere. Very very convenient as far as location goes with the hotel. Convenience store across the street came in handy as well as the BIG souvenir shop down the street. Subway down on Ashford for a cheap dinner was nice too. They had all kinds of nice little bar/restaurants on the water and also the fancier more expensive restaurants too like Ropa Vieja (Cuban) and Ajili Mojili (Puerto Rican I'm guessing). They also had a big Chili's on Ashford too. I am glad that I didn't stay in Isla Verde, too far off from everything but the airport. To get to the pool we had to cross the overpath, pass the casino, pass the Italian restaurant, walk through the cold, paint smelling pathway and take the elevator down. The elevator didn't work at times so we had to take the stars and instead of it going down to the Pool, it would go all the way up to the 10th floor and come back to the pool area. Very odd how the elevators work in the hotel. Must get that fixed!!! The pools were very nice and open all the time. They had one main pool and also a saltwater pool which seemed like a nice added touch. They need more lighting for the pool area at nighttime. Could barely see anything in the pool area at night which could be very dangerous for the kids. The jacuzzi was big and always available. The man at the front desk claimed that ALL of their rooms have been renovated which seemed to be true. Hopefully in a year all the contruction will be done and everything will be working properly and open. If not other hotels down the street would be an option for sure next time! PUERTO RICO is absolutely beautiful and can't wait to come back again!!!

<Author>MDDay
<Content>Overall good experience After reading reviews I almost changed my hotel, but in the end, The Condado Plaza was a good experience for me. Yes, it is under construction, but so is all of San Juan. I was very inmpressed with the friendly staff. After my first breakfast, the waiter recognized me every morning,as well as my waitress at the pool restaurant. I highly recommend the lobster benedict and the catch of the day at the pool restaurant was the best meal I had in San Juan. I had no problems with my room, great view, very clean and stylish. All the rooms are finished and I think it will be a beautiful hotel when renovations are. If you are out during the day as I was, the construction will not affect you. It just that the public areas are not very pretty at this time. If this will be your only trip to San Juan, you might want to stay somewhere else, but the location was great. Other hotels, like the Ritz, etc. were very far from all the action. I liked that The Condado is in walking distance to many restaurants, clubs and shoppping and a short cab ride to old San Juan.

<Author>edm7583
<Content>"Absolutely Amazing" Just got back from my 4th of July getaway to San Juan and I stayed at the Condado Plaza Hotel. A decision I didn't regret. It is the low season, and I got an amazing rate of $99 plus all taxes and fees. (note that the taxes and fees are pretty hight. Puerto Rico has a 9% tax for hotels without a casino and 11% on hotels with casino. Also the Hotel charges a Resort Fee of a whopping 14% of the rate per day.)The location has its pros and cons. On the western end of the Condado, there is no real beach. There is a small beach that is public right outside the hotel. It's not a bad little beach, but not as nice as other beaches east. On the plus side, you can walk to anything in the Condado. and for Old San Juan or Isla Verde, there are always a lineup of taxis outside day and night. A better option is the bus. The B21 line runs right past the hotel. This line runs from Old San Juan to the Plaza Las Americas mall, so it's easy access to both of these areas. To get to Isla Verde, take a taxi or a 15 minute or so walk to Ponce de Leon avenue and catch the A5 bus to Isla Verde. Remember all bus service stops around 9pm. They are renovating the hotel. Most of it is done, but the lobby and common areas in the main building are still being worked on. You have to enter and at the Lagoon Building across the street where the front desk is temporarily located and take the walkway to the main building's 2nd floor to access the casino, restaurants, and rooms. The rooms are absolutely enormous. I got a room on the 10th floor with the view of the lagoon, Miramar, and the mountains, and it is a gorgeous view. The rooms on the ocean view side of the hotel have balconies and are much more pricey. The room had a sofa and living room area, and a king size bed. the bathroom was equally gigantic, with a glass walk in shower stall right in the center of the bathroom. The shower stall could easily fit 3 people in it with room to spare! In the separate dressing area of the bathroom was the closet and drawers, with iron and board, and a small counter with coffeemaker and a refrigerator underneath. The other side of the bathroom had a huge marble counter with sink and hairdryer. Every amenity imaginable was in this room. Internet connection, plasma screen tv, huge marble desk, down bedding and comforters, and the enormous window that took up the whole wall giving a beautiful view of the highrises of Miramar and the mountains in the distance. Service is fantastic in this hotel! Everyone is very friendly and bends over backwards to help you.The casino is pretty nice too. One of the larger casinos in Puerto Rico, this still is nothing in size compared to the casinos of Vegas. There are about a dozen or so table games, and the rest is slots.However, what it lacks in size it makes up for with quick friendly drink service, friendly dealers, a smoke-free environment, and much lower minimum bets than in the high-end casinos in Vegas.Since there is not a huge, beautiful beach on premises, this hotel goes out of their way to make their pool area and gardens as nice as possible. There are 2 pools in the main building, and beautiful gardens with hammocks overlooking the ocean. Pool service is quick and friendly. Food is not bad at all but the restaurants and drinks are really overpriced. Eat elsewhere if you can. Overall, this hotel is best described as a 5 star hotel in a 3 star location. No you are not in Isla Verde, but you are in a convenient area, the rooms are luxurious, and the service here is truly first class.  
<Date>Jul 5, 2007

<Content>Beautiful Rooms; Service not so good My companion and I have just returned from a 7 night stay at Condado Beach Hotel and Casino in San Juan, PR. The hotel is undergoing some renovation, but the work had minimal impact on our stay. The room was as described on the website. We were in one of the red rooms in the ocean tower. It had a view of the lagoon, and of the city of San Juan. The room was beautiful - very modern, the bed really comfortable, with high quality linens. The bathroom was large, with a glassed in shower. Room also had flat screen tv, coffee maker, iron, and safe. The balcony was large and came with 2 chairs and a small table. The housekeeping staff was very accommodating and kept the room immaculate. The only minor problems were that we had to ask for washcloths, and from the hotel photos, it looked like there were supposed to be bath robes, but there were none. No big deal. Ok, that's the good. Now the bad. We found the hotel staff to be not very accommodating, and most of the time acted as though it was a bother for them to be asked anything. This happened time and time again, from the bell staff to the front desk, concierge, pool and casino staff. Here is one example: the hotel has guest laundry; the change machine was not working. It was close to the pool, so I went to the pool bar to get change. NO! To the front desk. NO! To the casino - yes but not very happily. Four outlets before I could get a dollar's worth of quarters!!Also, everything in PR is extremely expensive. Drinks and food at the pool are ridiculously priced, and here again, the staff very mediocre. Tip: one of the best and cheapest things on the menu are the empanadillas.All in all, we found Puerto Rico to be not a very hospitable place. The past 2 vacations have been spent in Mexico, and the difference is amazing. In MX, we were made to feel like people were genuinely happy to see us, the prices were always reasonable, and food always good. My advice: skip PR altogether and go to Rivera Maya. Oh, and one last thing. We are not complaining or picky people, but our experience in PR was not a great one. I hope yours is better.

<Author>VAgirly
<Content>Great city hotel We stayed at the Condado Plaza from April 23-29, and overall had a great experience. Be prepared though..it is definitely a city hotel, and if you are looking for a quiet secluded getaway, stay outside San Juan. This is also a big conference hotel, and I would say not a particularly romantic getaway, but overall very nice.I thought they did a great job renovating the rooms; a bit of an Asian flair instead of your typical caribbean theme, very comfy beds (no wierd smell on our pillows), huge bathroom and about a 3x3x3 foot glass shower with amazing water pressure. The shower leak was not a leak, per se, but water seeps out between the door hinge. Not a problem..just put a towel down. We had no problems with a/c, or the safe. The only problem we had with the room was that we were in the ocean tower facing the street, on the 9th floor. Construction on the other building did not bother us at all, but the traffic could be heard even with the door closed. In fact, cars driving by were so noisy at 11:30 on Sat. night we had to close our door to go to sleep. I would spring for the ocean view so you can hear the waves instead of the traffic!The concierge's were both VERY helpful, recommended some great restaurants, and got us set up with a rental car just down the street which we took to El Yunque and Bacardi. I definitely recommend renting a car for this rather than doing the tours. Also, wear your swim suit and towel to El Yunque..you can swim in the waterfall!The beach was not as bad as some say..it was pretty empty except for one day when a bus load of small kids came by for about 1/2 hour. We just headed up to the pool, which was very nice. The beach is on the lagoon, so there are no waves to ride, and there is a bridge with a fair amount of traffic right next to the beach. It wasn't that bad, but if you want to walk for miles on a secluded beach, this was not the place. Other than the beach, the location of the hotel was great. Old San Juan was about a 35 minute walk, or there is local bus stop right next to the beach. If you walk down the block there are MANY great local restaurants...our favorite was ROPA VIEJA, a Cuban/Puerto Rican place that was always crowded just a little ways down from the hotel. The Italian restaurant at the hotel was good, and so was the pool restaurant. Personally, I thought the drinks at the pool bar were expensive and did not have very much alcohol in them. Here's a great tip....there is a little convenience store just next to the hotel. We got a jug of Bacardi at the distillery, and stocked up on mixers at the store and made our own drinks!! We also tended to grab breakfast either at that store or at Starbucks next to the lobby (very convenient). Oh, and be warned, its hard to find decaf coffee down there! Overall, I thought this was a great hotel!

<Content>February break The previous negative review has prompted me to respond. My college age daughter and I planned a short visit to Puerto Rico for her well deserved February break . Yes, the beach is public, and very small, however, it's not a surprise if one actually pays attention to the information provided by the hotel and tripadvisor. Before we left, we emailed the hotel to ask for a renovated room. It was lovely, clean and quiet, looking out over the ocean. I researched a couple of restaurants and checked with the professional and helpful concierge, Jean Pierre who would either agree or suggest another choice that my daughter might prefer. He would make the reservation and when we appeared at his desk, he would escort us to a taxi and give the driver the address. Delirio's, Dragonfly and Pikayo were all different and delicious. For breakfast, walk down the street and sip your tea or coffe at Hacienda Don Jose, where you can have eggs, toast, and OJ for around $5.00 or simply order tea and toast and read. It's a tiny neighborhood cafe where the windows open up over the ocean. (TripAdvisor idea, of course)..The Condado is really trying to please....and by the way, there is construction all over San Juan...a necessary part of keeping the city revitalized and beautiful. And, always take some time to do your travel research...it's so easy .

<Author>NYCobalt
<Content>Nice Hotel, Great Location My husband and I stayed here for a long weekend. We had an ocean view room with beautiful views! Room looked exactly like the pictures on the website.
