There were two pools: one that was really shallow but had a swim-up bar and slide for kids and another, salt-water pool that was deeper, probably 6-8 ft or so. The hotel is not very far from Old San Juan. My husband and I went into that area quite often. It was a quick and easy drive. <Content>Great time at the Condado My husband and I stayed at the Condado Plaza Hotel and Casino from 1/25-1/31/07. The hotel is under renovation but remained fairly quiet. The other restaurants in the hotel were closed with the exception of the italian restaurant where the service was much to be desired. There are many restaurants within walking distance that are good and much much cheaper. If you are looking for a nice moderately priced place for dinner you must try Ropa Veija right down the street, The food and service were superb and by far the best meals we had on the island. The location of this hotel is great only 10-15minutes from Old San Juan. TIP: take the bus the bus stop is right outside of the hotel and its only 75cents each way versus 12 each way for a taxi. As far as the beach goes it was okay. Its a public beach and is small and a little rocky. Overall we had a great time and you cant beat the price. I would probably return to this hotel again but would also keep an open mind about other hotels in the area as well.

<Author>stevilboy
<Content>You get what you pay for at the Condado My wife, nine year old daughter, seven year old son and I just spent four nights at the Candado plaza (we are from NJ). The room was cheap and the pool was fantastic. We are pretty seasoned island travelors and we did have a great time. However we are on the adventerous side and did our research beforehand and knew what we were getting into. The owners are fighting to maintain and renovate a giant Resort and they are losing the fight. This place needs big corporate Hotel money to survive. You could count on something breaking down. For us it was the main pool (which was a big bummer) but they fixed it and I tracked the fix from talking directly to the pool repair company (hotel/no straight answer). They needed a pump and of course the hotel didn't have an extra one or backup system. The main pool is THE attraction and if it ain't working just pack the kids up and move on. One of two elevators was off and on the whole stay and that made for long waits. I'm just warning the people who think they are staying at the El San Juan or something like Mandalay Bay. It ain't that at all. However there are great restaurants down the street that are stand alone operations with competive pricing and great quality. You can also just walk to Old San Juan and get some culture. The Beach at the Condado is a public thing on a questionable lagoon. But hey! Hundred bucks a night, great pool w/ a big slide that kept the kids going all day long. Clean rooms, great views, safe area, museums, forts, swim up bar, in room frig, bodega 100 feet away. Did I mention the pool? Hurry and get there before it falls in to the Ocean. We had fun and it was a very friendly place. Flip flops and your favorite button downs will do. You will find mostly locals at the dining establishments down the streets which is encouraging and they dress very well, however you might feel ridiculous with the official Bermuda uniform on if you know what I mean. Bottomline: Worth my money and vacation time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>OK, but a bit shabby Our family stayed at the Condado Plaza for a wedding, so we got the base group rate of $140, plus hotel  resort taxes for a total of $175 for an ocean-side view. The room was a decent size with a huge walk-in closet, dressing area, small refrigerator, bathroom and balcony. The hotel's undergoing renovation, as is much of the Condado area, so our furnishings were a little tattered and worn. The pools are nice, but beach access is very limited. The water is calm here, which is nice for small children, but not good for those looking to ride the waves or take long walks on the beach. Avoid the pricey and standard-fare hotel restaurants and walk over to the Cafe del Angel for delicious and well-priced Puerto Rican dishes, such as mofongo (mashed and fried plantains) with fish or shrimp. There's also good sushi across the street from the hotel. For a treat, there's a nice ice cream parlor in the hotel's mezzanine across from the casino. Parking is an extra $15/night, but you can rent a car from Charlie's down the street and pay only $5/night to park nearby. Taxis are expensive, but the Condado Plaza is closer to Old San Juan than the hotels in Isla Verde, though it's a trade-off, since the beaches are better there. Next time I'd stay in Old San Juan or Isla Verde as the Condado area currently does not have much to offer.

At the front desk I was greeted with one of the most sullen people I've ever encountered. She said she had no more lagoon view rooms available that were non-smoking, all she had was an oceanfront. I questioned her as she didn't say this would be the same price  she responded Did you hear me? I said I was putting you in an ocean front room. I really was surprised to be spoken to in this manner  even said  I'm sorry if I've said something to offend you, but the room change was necessary for my son's health. We went up to the room  it was less than spectacular. Yes, it had an oceanview, once you looked past the asphalt rooftops  dirty drain water. The balcony was standing room only. The door lock was broken (they repaired it ). The air conditioner was leaking green goo onto the carpet long enough that the carpet fibers were worn through to the backing. There was a water leak in the ceiling tiles in the bathroom  2 more stained areas (no longer leaking) in our room,  the furniture was badly scarred  missing some pieces of wood. Other people we knew (it was an annual business meeting for surveyors that brought us there) said there rooms were much nicer. I can only conclude the surly girl at the desk believes in retribution. Also both surveyor dinners that were included had poor choices of food  actually ran out of food which took at least 1/2 hour to replace. On the plus side the Condado is in a good location  the majority of the people we encountered were helpful  friendly. I would return to Puerto Rico, but not the Condado

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Exceeded expectations! Despite some recent reviews which praised the hotel, I still went there with some dread, wondering if I would be saddled with a dirty room, etc. I must say that we were very pleased overall and had a great vacation. We chose the Condado Plaza because the rest of the hotels closer to the airport had negative reviews about the noise level of the planes flying throughout the day.The hotel occupies two buildings on either side of Ashford Avenue, which are connected by a walk-way from the casino. The main building (the one with the lobby) is towards the ocean and the building opposite is towards the lagoon. I asked to be shown two rooms and got to see the City Vista rooms in both buildings. The room in the main building was definitely run-down, with very old carpeting and worn out furniture. I prayed that the second room would be better and it was! I can only surmise that the people who wrote unhappy reviews got to stay in the City Vista rooms in tne main building. FYI, all City Vista rooms face the opposite buliding and from some, you can get a glimpse of the sea.Like some reviews mentioned, the concierges are not very helpful and are standoffish, but not rude. One gave me false information once - I had asked how much a taxi cost to go to Old San Juan and he said I did not need a taxi and could just walk the distance as it was right around the corner and about a 5-10 minute walk. It was lucky I asked the bellman for specific directions, because it turned out that it was a 5-10 minute RIDE in the taxi! The Condado beach is a public one and can be accessed by walking through the hotel, past the pools, or by the road. There is a person there to help you with the chairs. If you are a guest of the hotel, you do not need to pay the $4.00 to rent chairs. There are locals, at the beach, but for me, that was a great part of the charm. Puerto Ricans like to vacation with their families and it was wonderful to hear a new language, even if I did not understand it!. The beach is small and you cannot walk anywhere as there are rocks that form a barrier. On the bright side this is exactly what makes it safe for children to swim in those waters and there are fish that fish that my daughter chased around. Because of the rocks, the sand is not fine and you can get a scratch or two if not careful. It didn't bother me and we all went barefoot. The pools were on the smaller side and it was difficult to get chairs around the pool if you got there late. But the water-slide was great fun and the size of the pool was not an issue for me. The baby-pool is more like a fountain, but I was happy to have my little one wading in it, while watching my elder one at the water-slide.Old San Juan is to the right of the hotel. To the left of the hotel a nice walk, with some interesting shops, restaurants and convenient stores. A mile or so down to the left, is a nice, lively area with lots of people and restaurants. That is where the Radisson and the Marriott are located. Eating out is very expensive. We tried to find cheaper places to eat in, but the price in most places are fairly comparable. Since there is no sales tax on the island (good thing if you want to buy something from the Cartier, Dior close by), I suspect, restaurants make up for it. We were thankful to have Subway round the corner from the hotel and stocked up on snacks, orange juice and milk.Maid service was regular and a couple of requests we had were met promptly. When we interrupted the service however (we came for a quick change, when the maid was cleaning the room) it never got finished.Check-in and check-out were fast and efficient.Sure the Ritz is better, but I would have spent $350 a night there, as opposed to $150 a night at the Condado plaza.I would definitely stay at the Condado Plaza again, if we were to come back to the San-Juan area of P.R. It's proximity to Old San Juan (a $12 taxi-ride each way), but removed from the hustle bustle of the same, is very attractive. We went there every evening to eat and even tried this place called La Bombonera (unadvertised by tourist guides) which is a great little place with inexpensive and ethnic food; it also had some great pastries. There is a bus-stop to the left of the hotel, a minute's walk, where you can take a bus to the old city for a mere 75 cents and save yourself a nice bundle if you had the time. I took it twice and the bus drops you off at the pier in Old San Juan. Puerto Rico is a lovely place and we will definitely be back to the island again. It is thanks to my fellow tripadvisors that I got information that was useful and if anyone has any question, please feel free to write to me at cleocap@hotmail.comHappy trails!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not nearly as bad as they say!! Just got back from a 5 night, 6 day stay at the Condado Plaza with 2 of my girlfriends and must say that this place was more than I expected given the mostly negative reviews on this site!We booked a room through the hotel's website (which ironically, still states that it's associated with the Wyndham chain) and were able to get a city view room at the rate of $195 per night with the AAA discount. Upon arrival, however, we inquired about the availability of ocean view rooms and were given a free upgrade to a room with a nice balcony on the 8th floor. No hassling required! I definitely recommend asking upon check-in....worst case scenario is that they say no and you're stuck with a view of the lagoon. Though I must say that it is quite nice to sip your morning coffee on the balcony while watching and listening to the waves crash on the rocks. Overall, the room was average. We were 3 girls in the room with plenty of luggage in tow, so the enormous walk-in closet came in extremely handy. There was also a bar with not one, but two fridges in it, which we used to store a couple of bottles of wine that we bought from the convenience store next door. The bathroom was also average, though our tub did have the tendency to clog. We called housekeeping on the second day and they immediately sent up a repair man who fixed the problem. Service was below average. Although housekeeping was very pleasant and responed immediately to extra towel, extra pillow, and extra hair-dryer requests, the other other hotel staff was not very helpful nor very friendly. The concierge staff was quite rude, and though they did make a few dinner reservations in Old San Juan for us, they did so somewhat reluctantly. The young lady at the tour desk was extremely haughty and relatively uninformed regarding the various trips they had to offer. In addition, the staff in the various restaurants spoke limited English and were not very attentive. The pool and beach area were also below average. There were plenty of chairs and a nice poolside bar, though the pools themselves were extremely small and had a lot of debris in them. We walked onto the beach one day to check it out and immediately walked off. Although the water was warm and seemed clear, the sand was kind of dirty and had a lot of locals on it. Definitely no privacy or sense of calm. Of note, access to the hotel from this public beach is guarded by hotel security, who require that you show either your room key or the wrist band that they give out at the towel stand. Security also patrolled the pool area regularly and promptly removed people who were not patrons of the hotel. The food at the pool bar is extremely expensive! A salad there is $18...the same exact salad at the Italian restaurant on the Mezzanine level is $4.95. Definitely worth the short trip upstairs. We spent most of our pool/beach days at the Caribe Hilton which is right across the lagoon and is accessible via a short walk across the bridge. Our friend gave us his Hilton Honors card, so we were able to walk right into the hotel, get towels, use the facilities, etc. The pool and beach area is 100 times nicer at the Caribe Hilton than at the Condado Plaza, but at a rate of $400 a night, I think our strategy was better! The Caribe Hilton also has a very nice spa (1 hour massages in the $120-150 range) and a beautiful Pan Asian restaurant called the Lemongrass Grill. Definitely on the expensive side ($25-30 per entree), but the food and the ambiance seemed well worth it (I personally don't know how much our bill came to since our friend knows the owner, who came over and sat with us for the majority of the meal and then waived the bill!!!) The Caribe Hilton also has a Starbucks in its lobby, which we visited quite frequently!In terms of other restaurants in the Condado area, there is a nice Cuban/Puerto Rican restaurant called Ropa Vieja that's about a 3 minute walk from the Hotel. Very large portions and very reasonably priced (Our bill with appetizers and wine came to about $65 in total). I also recommend checking out Calle Fortaleza in Old San Juan which has a ton of really good restaurants. Lastly, the gym at the hotel was pretty nice...4 treadmills, 4 stationary bikes, and a whole slew of weight machines and free weights. There's a sign on the door that says a $7 fee will be automatically charged to your account once you swipe your hotel room key to get in, but no such charges showed up on our bill upon check-out. There is, however, a standard $48 per night resort fee/resort tax that is automatically charged to your account, so beware that you actually need to add on about $50 to the rate they initially quote you.Overall, the hotel superceded my expectations, though after staying at the Ritz Carlton on a previous trip to Puerto Rico and seeing the Caribe Hilton, I doubt I'd go back.Hope this was helpful!

<Content>Expensive so watch out I stayed at the Condado Plaza for two separate nights. The first time I was in the building on the lagoon side, with a beautiful view over the water. Once connected it worked fine. I had no issues with hotel staff, and check-in and check-out were easy. I walked by the casino but didn't linger because I don't like smokey areas. The Condado Beach area is OK, but if you want a beautiful long white sandy beach I would stay elsewhere. The area is convenient to Old San Juan, about a $12 taxi ride away.There are lots of hotels in San Juan, so next time I will try someplace different.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Better than expected except for tariff surprise Arrived at the hotel and entrance was nice. Once at the desk they made me sign an additional agreement which would bite me upon checkout. I'd recommend checking off that you will only pay for the hotel and phone calls but refuse to pay the additional tax and tariff since with my package via priceline it states taxes are included. On the day of checkout they'll slip a bill under your door insisting that you pay tax and tariff which amounted to an additional $160 for a 4 day stay. I disputed the charge and they agreed to wave the tax but said I still owed the $23/day tariff.Generally staff and puerto ricans were very friendly and I felt safe in Condado and Old San Juan with only 3 beggars seen the entire trip. On the ride to the Rain Forest you'll see very primitive living conditions and even within the city they have housing projects. Everything in Condado is gated, especially the condos and businesses. The hotel lobby was very nice with a cool salt water fish tank housing the laziest 3 sharks I've ever seen. There are about 5 restaurants within the hotel, the only one I'd recommend is Tony Roma's since prices are in line with other U.S. locations. Generally service at all of the restaurants we visited was slow so you'll need some patients. Meals at the other 4 hotel restaurants are very overpriced but if you want the convenience then go ahead. The location is prime and there are plenty of reasonably priced places to eat within a short walking distance along Ashford ave. I'd recommend Waikiki and Don Hose Hacienda which offer an incredible ocean view but if you go at night bring a light sweater. We got lucky at the casino: plenty of 1 and 5 cent slots to occupy your time.Room was acceptable with a good view of the lagoon and some basic patio furniture. The bathroom was a little small but generally very pleased with the room. No extra charge for using the safe. Cleaning staff were great: we even left out some cash and it was all there upon returning. No minibar in the room. As for the pools: there's a regular pool in the rear of the older lagoon view rooms part of the hotel which was barely used and we did some laps here without being disturbed. For more action, in the rear of the newer half of the hotel are two additional pools. These are busier and I'd recommend coming before 10 am for your lawn chair otherwise you could be waiting to snag one. The saltwater pool had plenty of sun bathers surrounding it but I didn't actually see anyone swimming in it. The other freshwater pool had a swim up bar and a section for kids. Drinks were about $8 and a little watered down so few people were actually purchasing. There is a small beach whereby they give you a free lawn chair to use. It's a little rocky and the locals do invade a portion of it so I wouldn't say it's anything special. The water is a little rough but not a bad change of venue. Did not see anyone Kayaking, snorking or SCUBA diving on Condado beach.To get to old San Juan you can take a bus for about $1 or just walk it since it takes about 1 hour to get there. It's well worth the time with plenty of shops and historic sites. This is where they let off all the cruise goers so it can get hectic.For day trips the hotel offers a tour operator (GSI) in the main lobby with several trip options. We did the Bacardi/Old San Juan tour hosted by Robert who was terrific and I'd highly recommend it for about $45 including 2 free drinks at Bacardi and admission to the Fort which was fascinating. We also went on the Rain Forest (El Yunke)/ beach day tour which was also a great way to spend a day for about $60. Plenty to see though the visibility of the water at the beach was about 5 feet so I felt that bringing my snorkling gear was a waste. We also went to Las Plazas Americanas which was a $15 cab ride to the biggest mall in the Caribbean, the biggest I've ever seen. Not a lot of deals but a good way to kill some time. One thing I noticed along Ashford was the incredible number of joggers. It was a great place to have a relaxing drink and people watch at the numerous streetside bars and restaurants. Overall I was initially worried by some of the reviews but was very pleased with the hotel. I would have preferred if they were more upfront about the tax and tariff but otherwise a big two thumbs up. We recommended the hotel to our in laws who will be going in the next few months. The beaches are less than average compared to other caribbean islands but there is a lot of action there and plenty of American chain restaurants it you are worried about food consistancy.

We also picked up some snacks and brought soda and snacks down to the pool in the afternoon.I'd stay here again if I wanted a quick getaway and got another good deal.

<Author>Agent011
<Content>Nice getaway place My wife and me just recently came back from a 7-night vacation. We have to say that Condado Plaza is a great hotel for a three star rating. Check-in was pretty quick and we didn't wait for the room at all. We asked for a possible free upgrade but the lady was unbreakable. She offered oceanview room for additional $40 per night. We declined. Our room was on the 9th floor. Hotel has 10 floors altogether and the top two floors are Executive level. Room was big with pullout sofabed and high speed internet modem. Comparing to other islands in the Caribbean, hotel food was not so expensive but was not worth money paid. Along Ashford Avenue, there are a lot of restaurants and fast food places that offer much more delicious meals. We usually had breakfast at Hacienda Don Jose which is like 2 minute walk from the hotel. It offers breakfast specials for $5.75. Right next door, there is Waikiki Restaurant  Bar that is a bit more expensive but steaks there are great. Both restaurants offer magnificent oceanview. On the other hand, staff of Condado Plaza did not look very knowledgeable about their own hotel. For example, one of the staff didn't even know where the third pool is. Also, do not leave your chairs unattended for too long. We left towels once to reserve spot and went for lunch. When we came back after an hour, the towels were gone. Hotel beach was clean and nice. If you love to play tennis, you may take advantage of this. They charge you $10 for reservation and $5 more for racquet and balls rental. So, if you bring your own eqipment, you may even play for free. Both courts are lighted. Nightly entertainment was boring. There was a live band playing right next to the casino. Unless you stood close to them, you couldn't hear them play. Marriot Hotel has live band playing every night from Wednesday to Sunday. It's just a 15 minute walk from Condado Plaza. Overall, we had a great time and we are satisfied what we got for our money.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Condado was OK I just got back from a 5-night stay at Condado Plaza in San Juan Puerto Rico. I felt the need to come on here and write about my stay to clarify some things. When I booked this hotel, I came on here and read some of the reviews and they were awful. I came in to the hotel trying to keep an open mind. The hotel honestly was average... I am a clean freak so there was nothing dirty about this hotel like some people have said in these reviews. The cleaning ladies were very nice and did a great job. The rooms were very clean as well as the bathrooms. The service however was definitely poor. I had to wait about 3 hours for my room to be ready and it took about an hour to check in to the hotel itself. The casino .. I would not recommend playing blackjack or slot machines.. I never saw anything hit. I play poker a lot (usually No Limit here in the US) and found that Puerto Rico only offers 5-10 Limit !! So I tried it out and it's a totally different game..but I made $600 on the trip playing this .. If you are a poker fanatic, take a drive over to Intercontinental to play..there are better players. As for the cuisine, I didn't eat in the hotel....the hotel's food was extremely overpriced! All you have to do to get some FANTASTIC food is walk about 5 minutes down the street from the hotel... and there are 2 great restuarants I went to called ROPA VIEJA and AJILI MOJILI They are excellent..also down that road is a Louis Vuitton store, a Cartier store and other nice shops... which made me happy :) Overall, It was a good stay.. nothing was dirty about the rooms or the pool area like previous reviews had said. It's just a place to stay and it definitely mett my expectations.

<Author>cocanat
<Content>Well worth it My wife and I just got back from a week in Puerto Rico (Nov. 3-10) and stayed at the Condado Plaza Hotel and we thought it was a great hotel.Since I think these reviews should start out with a short bio on the author, my wife and I are in our mid-50s, very middle class. We take a couple of travel vacations a year, and have become fairly skilled at finding the best accomodations for the money. The Condado Plaza seemed to be the best value, so we booked it, even though some of the reviewers have been brutal to this hotel.We booked a city view room and were pleased to find that all the city view rooms have a nice view of the ocean/lagoon/Old San Juan from the balcony. It wasn't as great as the ocean view, but we saved about $50 a day by booking the city view room. Facilities:The restaurants seemed to be nice, but the only one we ate in was Tony Roma's. If you like Tony Roma's in other locations (and we do), you'll like this one just fine. We generally just have one meal a day, and we discovered a half dozen very nice restaurants less than a quarter mile walk down Ashford Avenue. The two pools next to the beach at the hotel are beautiful, and one has a swim-up bar. There is a large hot tub in the pool area. The beach area is modest in size, but it's the calmest point in the Condado area. Note, if you're staying on the Condado at any place other than the Condado Plaza, you'll just be able to watch the ocean, not swim in it. If a great beach is what you are looking for, then stay in one of the hotels in the Isla Verde area. The beach there will satisfy anyone, but you'll be paying a lot more to stay out there. Casino...we went to several in San Juan, and the one at the Condado Plaza was the busiest. They have a Texas Hold-em Table going from about 6PM until the game breaks up, usually about 3AM. Just believe me when I tell you that you can make enough money here to pay for your trip if you are a skilled player. Overall, the casino was extremely satisfactory, with a good live band playing adjacent to it. In general, you must understand that the Condado Plaza is about 40 years old, built just after Castro took over in Cuba in order to fill the need for a classy Caribbean resort. The overall facility is excellent, just dated. The electric and plumbing worked just fine. The room was ample, the furniture was nice. The bathroom was modest, as in all the older hotels, but the closet was the best one I've ever had in all my travels. There is a safe in the room, and our unit had two small refrigerators. I found the poor reviews of this hotel to be either ridiculous, or from people who stayed at the wrong hotel in the first place. If you have a large budget, plan to spend the entire trip in your hotel, want the newest facility and the most dazzling beach, then book the InterContinental, the El San Juan, or the Ritz-Carlton. But if you're getting a nice price break, I think you'll enjoy the Condado Plaza Hotel. We liked Puerto Rico and plan to return in a couple of years. We will probably stay at the Condado Plaza again.  
<Date>Nov 18, 2005

Furthermore, everything in the room still has the Wyndham name on it. I thought that was funny. And, it if matters to some guests, the use of the hotel gym will incur you an additional daily charge.The hotel check-in clerk initially told me you don't have a deluxe room. When I showed her the confirmation print-out showing my reservation to be a deluxe room the clerk said nothing further. In fact, I found the clerk's attitude to be quite curt. In this business, attitude is everything and I give the check-in clerk very low marks. She apparently got annoyed when I wanted to know how much was the additional charge to get a room with an upgraded view.The floors where the guests rooms are have visibly worn hallway carpeting. The guest room itself was decent and spacious. Nothing spectacular. The walk-in closet was a nice surprise but the small bathroom was slightly disappointing. If you spend under $100 a nite it's fair. Anything over $125 per night is not a great deal at all (there is a hotel tax and a resort tax, totaling about 22% of the bill).At the end of the stay the hotel gave me a bill for the entire room even though my stay was prepaid through a package deak. Another minor inconvenience. Overall, it was a nice stay, nothing spectacular and certainly nothing extraordinary.By the way, if you are in the Condado area I cannot recommend eating Japanese food at Hamasaki. <Content>It was average My friend and I (both single girls in our 20's) just got back from PR last night. We stayed at the Wyndham Condado. The hotel is not as bad as some people have said on here. The Condado area is very old and is under construction. This hotel is located at one end of Condado by a bridge. The pictures of the pool on the website are a bit misleading. I only saw two pools.....one has a swim up bar but there was a TON of kids in it. The other is a salt water pool where it has more adults. The pools are not in the best condition. The beach is very very small. It's more like a swamp. The rooms are not bad. They have a huge walk in closet. The bathrooms are updated. We joined Wyndham By Request and got upgraded to a ocean front room which is beautiful at night so make sure you join. Right when you walk into the lobby you can smell smoke. The lobby is not bad though.....nice fish tank. Check in and out was easy. We arrived early and left late but the concierge held our bags without a problem. The service was wonderful and everyone was very nice. The casino is small. The pictures make it look larger. I didn't win (actually lost $200) and I didn't hear other people winning. It is open 24 hours. I did not eat at any of the restaurants there. For breakfast, I would suggest the Hacienda which is right down the street (maybe a block). The view is unbelievable. There is a Subway Subs right down the street also if you want something quick (and don't mind eating at a place that they have everywhere in the world). There is an amazing restaurant called Ajili Mojili which is down the street on the opposite side (Lagoon side). It is really good and the prices are reasonable. As for the nightlife.....we went into Old San Juan to a place called the Pool Palace. It had salsa dancing one night and another night there was a band. We also went to El San Juan (in Isla Verde) on Saturday night and that was pretty happening. It also has great looking people. Everyone is in the lobby dancing and hanging out.For beaches.......definately go to Isla Verde. You can take the bus......B21 to A5 (I think). It's $.25 each way/each bus. It is a bit of a ride and very crowded. We bused it there and cab'd it back ($13). As I mentioned, the beach by the hotel is very small (and it is a public) but is ok for a quick dip. I referred to it as the swamp. For activities.....The only thing we did was snorkeling. It was amazing! The company was called Spread Eagle II. Their website is snorkelpr. The price is $65 and that includes food which was amazing also. The captian, Tito, was great.....not to mention great looking! :) The other staff on the boat was wonderful also. I also heard the bioluminescient bay tour is really cool but we didn't get a chance to go.We had a great time and the hotel was fine. It was def. a three star hotel. If you want luxury stay at the El San Juan (also owned by Wyndham). It is pricier though. I would not recommend this place for a romantic getaway. There also was not a lot of singles. This hotel is probably better for families. I am def. going back to PR and would stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Place I stayed at the Wyndham Condado from 6-30 to 7-11. It was a wonderful stay. The staff was very attentive and helpful. The rooms were ample and had a huge closet, which could fit a twin size bed if needed. We were on the 7th floor ocean side. The building by the lagoon had ceiling fans, our side did not. This was not needed since the air conditioning was very good. At night I would make the room very cold and then prop the balcony door opened so that we could listen to the ocean throughout the night. It was a great way to sleep. We had a hard time trying to find a car rental from the places nearby, so the concierge immedialtely called a dealership that would rent cars. We got a better deal then what Avis and LM were offering. LM require that you show proof of car insurance if you choose not to take their ins. Of course we did not have our cards with us. Besides their rates were outrageous. The staff were always helpful when it came to giving us directions. They were always ready to open the doors and take luggage.The building is old, so expect some things to be a little runned down. Many people have complained about that the carpeting is old. If People are concerned about carpeting then go somewhere else. This should be the least of your concerns while on vacation. So what if the carpeting is old. You go on vacation to enjoy the sights, the pool and to eat. Not to look at carpeting! The elevators at times were slow, so don't try taking the elevator during checkout time, that is when they are slow, but otherwise they were fine. The pool area was very nice. People complain about too many kids in the pool, but what can you expect, the pool is 3.8ft deep, of course all the small kids are going to be there. It seems to me that these people just don't understand that families go on vacation too, so there are going to be kids. If they they do not want to see so many kids then go to an adult only resort. Leave the rest for those of us who have children. We got to swim in the pool at anytime. Sometimes we were out there until 2am. You simply had to bring your own towels. Staying at the hotel was Rosalyn Sanchez (rush hour) and Shannon Elizabeth (american pie). They seemed to enjoy the hotel also. Some people complain that this is not a 4 star hotel. For the price $(140) it was a very nice hotel. If you want 4 Star then you have to be willling to pay $300 or $400 a night. Some people who checked in after the 4th of July got ratges at $90. I don't know about you but I would rather spend my money on other things than to shell out $5000 just for a hotel. If you want 4 star then go the Ritz or Intercontinental. The area is under a lot of construction. You have to realize that the Condado area was built in the 1960's. So yes, the area is looking a little outdated. But they are working on that. They are currently rehabbing two hotels along the strip. These will be beautiful when completed. Don't expect it to look like Las Vegas, this is an old island and they sre suceptible to hurricanes and wear and tear from the ocean. During the 70's this was a very happening place, and when all of the construction is completed it will be like that again. I think it is still very happeing, on Fri and Sat evenings all of Ashford Ave. is filled with people going out to have a good time. Plenty of outdoor Cafes offering music and drinks. It is very lively and beautiful at night. You don't have to stay in the hotel, it is very safe with plenty of police all around.We never ate at the hotel. I knew the food would be expensive. Instead we would go walking down Ashford Ave. There are plenty of places to choose from. If you don't mind paying a lot for Puerto Rican food then go to Ajili Mojili, or Ropa Vieja. Puerto Rican food is not expensive, so we chose not to eat there. Instead we went to Cafe Angel and the Godfather 3. Their prices were much more reasonable and authentic. In Old San Juan go to El Jibarito on Calle Sol. Excellent food and prices.Yerba Buena has a cuban group that plays excellent music on Fridays nights. They give the audience instruments so that they can participate in the music. I loved the music. There is dancing also if you choose to. This is a Cuban rest. I went for the music and the drinking, so I didn't eat there. My sister did and she loved the food. I have plenty of pictures if you would like to see them then just email me I will send them to you.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I liked this hotel! I had a great time at this hotel. I stayed for 2 nights at the Marriott for business but moved the Wyndham Condado the last 2 nights because they were cheaper. I was very happy with the deluxe room (same online AAA booking price as a standard room) that I had because it was more than I needed and it was nicer and more spacious then the room that I had at the Marriott. My room had the bedroom as well as living room, and the bathroom was off the short hallway that joined the two other rooms. There was also a TV in each room, separate climate control for the 2 rooms, internet, 3 phones, mini-fridge, safe, minibar, ceiling fan, standard coffee maker, hair dryer, iron/ironing board in room. The room was clean and well furnished with potted plants, and the sofa in the living room was a sofa bed...and I never caught a whiff of cigarette smoke on my floor or in my room. My view was of the Ocean Side building of the hotel across the street, but past that I could also see the ocean and to the left the lagoon. On the flipside, some other people who were on the trip with me also got a room at the Wyndham Condado, but they were in the other wing of the hotel Ocean Side. Their room was a standard and didn't look as nice- ample space but all the furniture just looked older. Their ice machine didn't work and they complained about the parking and how no one offered to help them with their bags right away. This may explain the mixed reviews that this hotel has gotten.Other things about this hotel: -Pool area on the Ocean Side has a swim-up bar, a water slide, several pools (including saltwater one), hot tub, loads of lounge chairs, hammocks, and is literally separated from the beach by 3 steps. The beach area that adjoins it is small but not too crowded even the 4th of July weekend I was there, was relatively clean (Wyndham staff cleans the area abutting the resort), and there is a wave break that stills the water to a gentle lapping...fish swim right up to your feet in the clear water. -Live Latin music on the small stage near the casino every night I was there...you can dance if you want to.-A lively casino atmosphere and plenty of restaurants in the hotel to choose from.-The lobby has an aquarium the length of a wall, huge mosaics of mermaids, and colorful blown glass light fixtures in the lobby and on the Mezzanine level.-Gusto di Italia- food was okay and prices comparable to Olive Garden, but the service was fantastic. The waiters were very attentive and super nice. Skip Coqui Shack by the pool. The food was not worth, even the $6-something for the breakfast buffet- there are so many other better, cheaper options on Ashford. Other recommendations: Take the bus for 25 cents instead of a cab for $12-$14 each way to Old San Juan or Isla verde. Eat at the Parrot Club in Old San Juan (~$23/entree but worth it). Speak Spanish if you can just because it's a great chance to practice and people are so nice, no one will make fun of you. You can always fall back on English since everyone speaks that too. Also expect: Tropical heat/humidity, crazy driving, music everywhere and police cars that always flash their lights (but not their sirens) even when they aren't trying to pull someone over. This is just the way things are on the island.

I called about our TV twice and both times had someone at our door in 10 minutes. At check out, there were some discrepancies with our bill but those were taken care of immediately. Overall we had an absolutely great time in Puerto Rico and I'm looking forward to going again. For a good price (under $150 per night) I'd definitely stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great stay and nice time My husband and I recently returned from the Wyndham Condado last week, June 5-10th. We had an absolute fabulous stay at this hotel. Below are several tips on getting the most for your $$ while on vacation. Upon arrival in San Juan we took a 10 minute taxi ride from the airport to the hotel for $12 total. The hotel is in the tourist zone so the taxis have increasing fees for various zones (this is zone 3 and not bad for the money). I should also note the taxis have a minimum charge of $3/person. When we arrived at the hotel we checked in with our Wyndham By Request # (signup for this program online before your trip as it definitely has its advantages). Although we book our trip through Expedia -in which the program doesn't apply to online bookings (only through travel agents, Wyndham reservations or tour companies) - we were still upgraded to an oceanfront room free of charge and complimentary soda and snacks were placed in our room the next day by housekeeping (part of your preferences w/the program). The room is nice and spacious - parlor, walk-in closet w/safe, bathroom, queen bed w/sofa sleeper and balcony. There's a beautiful view of the ocean. The pools had a steady flow of people during the day; however, the pool bar was always empty. A lot of the guests, as well as my husband, took luxury in relaxing in the lagoon right outside the main pool. The beach advertised in the photos is a very small public beach (all beaches in Puerto Rico are public and access is open to all). During the week it was not very crowded and there's plenty of fish swimming up to you - so feel free to snorkel. The grounds are well manicured and very secure. The hotel restaurants are EXTREMELY, EXTREMELY expensive. However, this is easily remedied by venturing outside the hotel. To the left and about 1 block 鈥?1 mile away there are several restaurants which you can find good deals (Waikiki, Chilis, Subway, Wendys, Pizza Hut), and for authentic Puerto Rican food (Ropa Vega, Ajoli Mojoli, Caf茅 De Angel). We also ate dinner at Tony Romas which wasn't very expensive (spent about $50). There is a Walgreens (near the Marriott) and Liquor Store down this strip to get snacks, pop and water to store in the small in-room refrigerator. The hotel charges $7 for one bottle of beer but you鈥檙e better off paying $10.99 for a six pack at the store. The casino is nice and has a steady stream of customers. However, neither my husband nor I are gamblers so we didn鈥檛 venture much in this realm. Another interesting tip if you鈥檙e going into Old San Juan just take Bus 21 and pay .25垄 for the 10-15 minute ride. It runs about every 30 minutes and stops right outside the hotel. A good place to eat is Barrachina 鈥淗ome of the Pina Colada鈥?on Fortaleza St. They'll give you a small sample of their world famous pina colada. As for excursions, the El Yunque tour ($45) is well worth the money as a guide drives you and other couples along the coast east to Fajardo. You鈥檒l see a lot more of the island and learn some good historical information along the way. The Bacardi Rum Tour is overpriced and can be done for much cheaper. Again, take Bus 21 (.25垄) to Old San Juan then go to Pier #2 to take the Ferry (.50垄) to Cantaneo. Once there pay $3/person for the taxi to the Bacardi distillery which is free to enter plus each person gets two free drink tickets. In total we paid $15 roundtrip for the both of us. While at the plant you鈥檒l have to chance to purchase rum and lots of it at a really cheap price (except Bacardi 151 it won鈥檛 be allowed on the plane). ALL IN ALL, WE REALLY ENJOYED OUR TRIP, THE HOTEL AND PUERTO RICO. I HOPE THESE TIPS HELP WITH YOUR VACATION PLANNING AS I KNOW TRIPADVISOR DID WHEN WE PLANNED OURS.

<Author>Cheesehead1
<Content>Not bad, not great The Condado area and the Wyndham Condado Plaza are a little tired and past their prime, but the location is convenient for business or tourism. Service was nothing special but not terrible. This hotel is not up to mainland Wyndham standards, true for all PR hotels I've stayed in.The restaurant has an excellent view of the ocean with waves crashing in, but there is no beach facing the ocean (rocks). The food in the restaurant was passable, but overpriced (as for most of San Juan), and the service was nothing special.There is a lot of construction as the PR government demolished the old convention center, replaced with a nice park and boardwalk, and is restoring two hotels, including La Concha (should have demolished it  started over). There is a huge new convention center being built across the bay from OSJ on an old military base.I stayed 3 nights at the Condado Plaza for a business trip. 19th floor room was OK and had a nice balcony and an enormous walk in closet. The hotel is on the end of the Condado hotel zone within view of Old San Juan and the fortress. There is a tiny beach area on one end of the hotel overlooking the bridge between Condado and Old San Juan (also under construction), and a decent pool area with fresh and salt water pools. Photo is taken from pool area. There are a number of restaurants and shops in walking distance, and a short cab ride to Old San Juan and the cruise port. I did not use the casino but it was cramped, crowded, smoky and tacky with an obnoxiously loud, bad salsa band.The beaches for most of the hotels on Condado are narrow, and not safe after dark. If you go toward the beach after dark, cops in body armor will shoo you back to the street. Ashford Avenue is safe and heavily patrolled, but the side streets are not recommended at night, and there is a large, dangerous public housing project between Condado and the freeway. If you are looking for beach action, stay in the Isla Verde area or at one of the all-inclusive resorts with private beaches. Old San Juan is much improved over the last 5 years and well worth touring, as is the fortress.

<Content>Was Pleasantly Surprised Just returned after a 5 day stay (Easter week) at the Hotel. Before my departure to PR, I read all the reviews on this hotel and was actually thinking about cancelling my reservations at the Wyndham Condado and staying elsewhere. However, I was pleasantly surprised. Our check-in was quick and the staff was courteous. Our room was not ready upon check-in and was told to return in about 1 hour. One hour later the room was ready and it was an ocean view room with a balcony. An upgrade from what I had paid for. Rooms are old but clean. I found restaurants in the hotel to be expensive. Definitely walk down the street and go to Ropa Vieja for authentic PR food. The mexican restaurant is great for breakfast and dinner and Wakiki next to the mexican restaurant is good also. Sit in the back and enjoy the ocean view. Good food and inexpensive compared to the hotel.The beach is nothing to talk about but we took a cab ride to Ocean Park Beach and it was beautiful. Wide clean beach and beautiful, wavy ocean. I do have a comment about the beach at the Wyndham and that is the guy who brings you your lounge chair. Talk about rude!!Pool area is nice, plenty of lounge chairs. If you want a drink, you are better off going to the bar yourself. Not enough waiters.We took the $.25 bus ride to Old San Juan. Nice shops, restaurants and visited El Morro. Nice day but plan on lots of walking, wear sneakers.Walk down Ashford to Walgreens and stock up on water, lotion, etc. Everything in and near the hotel is expensive. Lots of police presence so I always felt safe.All in all, we had a wonderful time and would return.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very enjoyable stay! Overall: We visited San Juan this March for 4 nights and stayed at the Wyndham Condado. Lovely experience at the Wyndham for the price, (booked on Expedia) comfortable rooms, good location, on a small beach, plenty of pools, lots of restaurants around. Good value for the price -- mid range family hotel in San Juan.Rooms - We paid for a City View, got a room in Laguna Towers (across the street from the lobby  beach), connected via casino hall, had a beautiful balcony overlooking the water. Definitely try to get a room with balcony that faces the water (also, perhaps I was upgraded through Wyndham By Request). The room was comfortable and perfectly adequate - upon close inspections some of the wood is chipped/scratched, but not a big deal. (I've stayed luxury hotels like the Mandarain/Ritz, it is NOT that, but neither are the prices.) Bathrooms were quite small and our phone did not work well, we tried to get someone to fix it, but it never really worked. However, not that important to us!Hotel - Tennis courts were $10/hr, we NEVER had a problem reserving or using a court. The pools were gorgeous although at one pool they had a DJ that was playiing music loudly, but we just went to another pool area. Plenty of chairs, umbrellas, towels, always available. The beach is quite small, so one day we spent the day there, the next day we took a $10 cab ride to Isla Verde to a larger beach. By the water sports area it took some time trying to rent a double kayak (first time we stopped they didn't have any available, second time we got one), but it was beautiful paddling around the lagoon. To check out, the service is quite slow, we stood in a long line, but we were so relaxed on vacation, we didn't care too much! The maids were fine (a little loud clanging in the hallways in the morning), pool waitstaff was perfectly nice.Food - We took the $0.25 bus ride to Old San Juan, visited El Morro and the other fort. We had lunch inside some local mall, very authentic Puertican food! Another place I would recommend for lunch (we never woke up in time for breakfast!) by the Wyndham Condado is a small Mexican place down the street, don't know name, but wonderful ocean view, terrific food (slow service) reasonable prices. We also visited Ajili Mojili for upscale PR food (average rating, expensive) and La Casita in Isla Verde (very good local food, cheap, moderate diner ambience), Tona Roma's in the hotel (good for American ribs! moderate prices), sushi in the hotel (pretty good too).Other - We also visited the Zen Spa near the hotel - great experience!! Very reasonable prices (at least vs. NYC) and had a lovely massage. Also, the concierge desk at the Wyndham was always swamped so I would research where you want to go before you get down there. We could not get into the DragonFly restaurant since we had not put our name on the waiting list, so I'd do that before!I would definitely recommend staying at the Wyndham Condado for a reasonably priced long weekend in San Juan! Not everything is perfect, but if you can roll with the small things (waiting in checkout line, waiting for concierge, broken phone), it's a pleasant stay for all the other aspects!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not too shabby My husband and I spent 5 nights at the Condado at the end of February 2005. I had previously read reviews on this website, and found them to be quite accurate. Definitely join Wyndham by Request (takes a few minutes online). I did and we were able to get a room upgrade from one facing the bay to an ocean view...definitely much nicer and wonderful to listen to the ocean at night. If you are looking for a beach resort, this is not the place for you. The beach is a tiny public area right next to a small bridge and not even worth going to. The pool area is very nice, though, and overlooks the sea. We were not impressed with the food at the pool grille. Service was slow and the food was disappointing, the hamburgers were inedible. Drinks were good, but there weren't enough waiters circulating the pool area and we usually had to go to the bar to get them. We ate in the Italian restaurant, and the food was good and very reasonably priced. We had breakfast in the Oceanfront place right next to the hotel, which was about $5 for a full b'fast and a lovely view of the sea. Also right outside of the hotel, Ropa Vieja was a great spot for an authentic and delicious dinner. In Old San Juan, we had dinner at Dragonfly, a trendy Asian-Spanish fusion place. It was very overpriced for tiny portions (ie. $24 for 6 scallops) and we were still hungry after leaving, but the atmosphere was enjoyable. If you need something in the hotel, service is very slow. There was no hairdryer in my room and I had to call 3 times and wait 50 minutes for someone to bring one up. Overall, I would say this is a mid-range hotel, not for a discriminating traveler, but a nice break from the cold New York winter.

<Author>Cheef45
<Content>Average Hotel - Above Average Rates I just returned from Puerto Rico. I wanted a quick getaway for me and my family. I chose the Wyndham Condado for the fact that the online photos of the place and description were very nice. Also for the fact that it had the most affordable rate for the busy week we traveled (Holy WeeK 3/21/05). My first impression was good. After we caught a cab from the taxi stand directly outside the airport we headed straight for the Wyndham which was a 10 minute drive. The hotel was decent and located in a seemingly busy area Condado. There are two different buildings with a clear tunnel connecting the two buildings. The side where we stayed was called the Lagoon and I am not sure what the other building was called. Check in was also decent although our room wasnt quite ready do to the early check in. Lucklly I had family already staying at the hotel at time of check in. I went up to see my other family's room. I have to be honest and say that i was NOT impressed at all. I thought the photos were a bit misleading. The rooms seemed to be old and dingy in appearance such as carpeting and furniture. Maybe it had to do with the building we were in but who knows. The room had a separate sitting area couch, TV, etc. The mini bar was unstocked even though it was mentioned that there is a mini bar in the room which will be replenished daily. There was a little balcony outside with a view of the streets below, a portion of the ocean, and the other building. MY room however was more like a suite i dont understand why because we both paid the same rate. The room was much better than that of my other family's. Much more roomier, and a much bigger balcony WITH a table and two chairs. Even though the building and rooms seemed old, there were good points. The bed was nice, the pillows were great, the bathrooms were clean and the shower is superb. The water pressure or the shower head was almost a massaging type of feeling. Very nice. SOmething you'd have to experience to understand. Our room was cleaned every day with bed made and towels, toiletries replenished daily. I didnt interact with much of the staff there but the staff hailing the cabs and greeting you were very friendly. The pool area is also nice. The view from out there was great. The scenery looked very nice. You can see the water crashing against the rocks right in front of you. This area is to the side of the pool where hammocks and long chairs were set up. The pool is on the other side of the building but you can easily commute through the tunnel. The beach is really nothing to talk about. I believe it is public so anyone can go there. But there is security at the entrace between the beach and the hotel property to limit entrance by non-hotel guests. Its very small and not very tempting. If you want to enjoy the PR beach then this place isnt recommended. This area is more of the city. I havent seen any reviews on the casino in this place. From first glance it doenst seem very big. but it is a really good size with a lot of machines and tables. When you actually enter and walk around you get the feel of the size. Again, everything seemed old though. The machines were old, the carpeting looked old. But they do pay. We had luck on the slots! I cant comment on the restaurants there. We ate out at the restaurants down the block from the hotel. I wanted Puerto Rican food. You HAVE to sample the local restaurants! Ever had Puerto Rican coffee? There is a Tony Roma's in the lobby of the Lagoon bldg. The service was great. I also noticed a japanese place but there were hardly anyone there. To sum everything up...I had a great time in Puerto Rico, loved the food and was content with the hotel. If you want a fabulous beach resort I wouldnt recommend it here. IF you wanted to come out have fun, enjoy more things outside the hotel and tour then this place should be taken into consideration, although I would have expected a nicer place for the money. Speaking of touring I recommend renting a car for a few nights, get a map and ask the staff for directions. The hotel tour prices were crazy and it only included basically going to and from different locations. I found every where very easily - We did the rainforest (great), Old San Juan (nice), and Belz outlet shopping (also nice). I hope this helps! Enjoy....

<Author>Whispy3
<Content>An honest review with helpful hints!! Just returned from the Wyndham Condado, March 9-13 and it definately served the purpose. We wanted a few days away from the cold and the snow, someplace that was close and had hot sunny days. The hotel is only 15 minutes from the airport, no problem getting a taxi at the airport. We are Wyndham By Request members and when we checked in they upgraded us to a junior suite, we originally just asked for a standard King. To be honest, we ended up seeing what a standard King room looked like and the set up of the room was nicer since we didn't use the front room with the table and chairs. The bathrooms are not designed well at all. Only one person can use it at a time. Now for some helpful hints... Try not to get a city (street) view room. The noise was not bad on Wednesday and Thursday night, but Friday and Saturday night were VERY noisy. Don't be afraid to walk into the town, (NOT OLD SAN JUAN), but the town where these hotels are. The street is Ashford avenue and we walked one evening for about a mile or so past the Marriott and it was VERY nice and SAFE. Lots of restaurants and plenty of police watching out. There is a Walgreens down that way and if you go one of your first days there, buy some bottled water there, only 99 cents compared to $2.00-$3.00 at the hotel. Don't eat at the Italian restaurant at the hotel. Definately venture out and experience the local places, excellent food. If you walk down near the Marriott the restaurants are busy and looked great, from Danny's Pizza to typical Puertorican cuisine. If you want to play tennis, as we did, make sure you play before 10:00AM. We played every morning, with no problem getting a court. There are two courts with lights, we never tried playing late in the day, but the heat in the morning is intense. The main pool area is GREAT, lots of chairs, a separate salt water pool, hammocks and lots of fun. Nothing nicer than sitting at the pool enjoying some food and drinks. Oh and speaking of food at the pool.... There is a Subway less than a block away and SOOOOO many people would go there and get some subs and return to the pool for lunch. The prices for food at the hotel are high. If you want a treat after dinner, the Ice Cream Parlor in the hotel is delicious!! Take a brownie sundae back to the room and enjoy!!

<Author>mguest
<Content>Pleasant Hotel My husband and I stayed at the Wyndham Condado Plaza for one night as a result of a American Airlines' flight delay that stranded us in San Juan. Although it was close to 12 midnight when we arrived at the hotel, the check in process was friendly and efficient. Upon our request for a non smoking, king size bed room, we were given a very nice corner room on the 8th floor in the hotel's Laguna Plaza tower. The room was large, comfortable, and clean. The room included a nice work desk with Aero chair, wrap around balcony, and the bathroom was stocked with Golden Door Spa toiletries and a coffee maker. Room service for late night dining, albeit quite limited, was fine; room service for breakfast was fine as well and both took more than 30 minutes to be delivered. Additionally, it was Saturday night and both the casino and music venues were going full force but the hotel has good sound proofing. For frazzled and tired travellers, the Wyndham Condado gave us a pleasant place to rest.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfectly satisfactory We had overall positive impressions on the hotel, but I think it all turns on how much you paid for your room. At $129 a night, with an ocean view, we thought it was a very good deal and were very happy with the amentities. Positives: Great views with nice balconies on the ocean-facing side. Very nice pool complex with lots of comfortable chairs, hammocks and a truly fabulous waterslide for kids (and the young at heart). Also, the service was friendly and hotel is very conveniently located (close to airport, old san juan and neighboring Ocean Park-- the nicest beach area around.) The 24 hour restaurant and casino are nice amenities. However, the place is not perfect and not quite up to the claimed four star ratings The rooms are a little bit worn. If there is a problem with your room, the service is-- again-- friendly, but SLOW. And the other negative is that, while the ocean views are nice, there is not much of a beach there. However, a easy 5 minute cab ride to Ocean Park, will bring you to WIDE, CLEAN expanses of lovely sandy beaches. (Try the area right in front of the Hostelria del Mar). So-- we had a nice time and were perfectly content; its simply a question of whether you feel are getting a good value for your money. We wouldn't have been satisfied with our experience if we were paying $200 or more.

<Author>BigAlFromDaBronx
<Content>Better Than I Expected After reading some of the reviews, I frantically tried to get another reservation elsewhere, but without success. So I expected the worse. The hotel is in a major city. Ashford Avenue is a major throughfare in the area. So of course the hotel is located on a street. So is any major hotel in any major city. The hotel is located at the tip of a penisula, with the Atlantic ocean forming the northern border of the hotel. We had a lovely room with a balcony and a very comfortable king size bed overlooking the lagoon. This was a southern exposure, so the balcony was engulfed in the sunshine all day. It was a great location to get to the Pan American cruise terminal, as Ashford Avenue becomes a causeway which leads to the terminal. The hotel was in excellent condition cosmetically, and very clean. The casino was lively with free entertainment along side the Casino. Drinks were priced on the high side, but very well prepared. There was a very reasonably priced Tony Roma's restaurant on the premises, as well as a very good ice cream shop. I am puzzled about the security issues raised in other reviews as the hotel was crowded, people were walking on the streets at night, and the room had its own individual safe. If the El San Juan and the Intercontinental are 4 stars, then this is a 3.5 in comparison. If you consider those 5 star hotels, then this was a 4 star hotel. <Author>lsvillekyguy
<Content>You get much less than you pay for at this property, they might even take more $$ than they deserve! Scheduling business in San Juan, I booked four nights at the Wyndham Condado Plaza (normally I stay at a resort in Dorado but wanted to stay closer to Old San Juan this time). Upon arrival I was upgraded to an ocean view at no extra charge which turned out to be the only truely positive aspect of my stay.My first visual impression of the property was that of a run-down resort in much need of renovation. Once reaching the room, that impression was solidified. The grounds, indoor and outdoor guest areas were much of the same, especially lacking in simple cleanliness (including the casino, main pool, outdoor bar  restaurant). The salt water pool and hot tub were closed. The small beach resembled the resort in it's lack of upkeep, abundance of trash and to reiterate one other review . . . it is practically part of the adjacent road. One of the evenings I dined in the main restaurant across from the casino, while the meal was not unsatisfactory (with the exception of being seated next to a walled column with more food stuck on it than what was plated), the service was. On another evening I ordered a Chicken Caesar Salad from room service, when it finally did arrive, the chicken had obviously been cooked hours earlier and was unfit to eat.Now to the real infractions, on my third day there Tropical Storm Jean hit. There was absolutely no notification to guests in any manner before, during or after the storm. For myself, a single traveler, any hotel response would have been appreciated and in my opinion necessary, a hotel's guests and their safety should have been the number one priority. The hotel made the mistake of boarding up fire exits which opened up to outside alcoves  enclosed stairways above the pool, unfortunately should there have been a fire at any location down any floor's west corridor, the only safe passage would have been to jump off of a balcony into 75+ mph winds! Oddly enough, the front doors to the resort where open and the hotel staff were allowing visitors to stand outside in the motor lobby while rather large debris blew right in front of them. On the same day, I was told by the restaurant manager that they had run out of food and due to the electricity outage could not cook anything else. I was lucky I'd had some carry on food  water from the plane trip especially as the mini-bar/refrigerator did not work adequately. Please keep in mind I could not leave the property, the hotel was my only source for food and beverage! The housekeeping staff put bags consisting of a bar of soap and a towel on our doors daily during the storm operation. Although no occupied rooms were cleaned, all vacant ones were to accommodate new guests!?!On what would have been my final evening there, I inquired regarding extending my stay as my flight had been canceled, they were quick to accomodate which I do thank them for. Unfortunately, I'd not slept well for the previous two stormy days and the hotel was operating under limited power so the air conditioning in the rooms was not working. The next morning I overheard another guest saying that Old San Juan was back up with full power so I inquired at the front desk if there was another Wyndham I could transfer to and be more comfortable. The young lady verified that the other Wyndham hotel was fully operational and said I was welcome to go to the other property. She also verified there would be no fees for early departure as I was relocating to another Wyndham for the sake of comfort and was leaving on my original departure day.I did so immediately (which happened to be shortly after check out time) and found an absolutely beautiful hotel, (Wyndham Old San Juan), a wonderfully clean and fresh guestroom, and immediately had a four course luncheon that was simply superb! To finish my story, the Wyndham Condado charged me for the last night in which I transferred to the other hotel. I have contacted everyone from the resort's credit manager, my credit card company, as well as Wyndham's Corporate Guest Staff regarding the double billing and have never received any contact. I've traveled back to San Juan since September (I go an average of three times a year) and stayed again at the hotel in Old San Juan I enjoyed that last evening ... ironically it's now an upscale Sheraton! Not surprising!

I would go back to this hotel if I had to, but I will probably stay at another part of PR, just to get closer to other sights outside of Old San Juan.

<Author>barney01
<Content>Neither horrible nor wonderful I have to say, after reading all the horrible reviews about this hotel, I was VERY trepidatious about staying here. I read such comments as, crowded, smoky lobby, rude, unhelpful staff, dirty rooms with mildewed carpet, etc. However, after being at the hotel for about 3 hours, my husband and I agreed that this was definitely a nice hotel, and we could not understand why there were so many negative reviews.The hotel is in the process of renovating, and if you go in understanding that, you're already ahead of the game. Our room was beautiful and had a great oceanfront balcony. (We may have stayed in one of the rooms that had already been renovated, but I'm not sure.) In any event, I have no complaints about the room. When I travel, all I really ask is that my hotel room is clean, reasonably nice, and receives daily attention from the housekeeping staff. All of these requirements were met with no problem. I am by no means a hotel snob, as I have stayed in plenty of budget- and moderately-priced hotels in my lifetime. However, I've also had a 10-day stay on the club level of the Ritz-Carlton San Juan, so my hotel stays have pretty much run the gamut. This hotel is certainly not the R-C, but it's not the complete opposite either. I've stayed in plenty of Wyndhams, and this hotel is on par with the rest of them. It IS an older hotel, but it IS nice, and it IS being renovated. I would stay there again with no hesitation.A couple of negatives, though. First, the beach is probably the smallest public beach I've ever been to. The hotel does indeed front the ocean, but the beach access is on the side of the hotel, and it is Condado Public Beach. It is a tiny beach with no waves. Basically, the beach is at the very beginning of the Condado Lagoon. It's very rocky, so if you want to get out in the water, bring water shoes. A lot of people in our group enjoyed snorkeling, though, because the waters were calmer than the ocean. I prefer waves and a larger beach, so that's why this was a negative for me. Also, drinks and food are unbelievably expensive in the Condado area, including at the hotel. My husband ordered a Medalla Light (local beer) from the hotel's swim-up bar. It came in a 10 oz. can (not 12 oz.) and was $7.00, which we thought was outrageous. If you stay here, just be prepared to shell out the dough if you eat or drink anywhere in the area. I had also read bad reviews about the pool area. Personally, I thought it was a very nice area, and there were lots of secluded spots to read, take a nap, etc. There's a saltwater pool, a freshwater pool, and a large jacuzzi. We enjoyed the pool area and have no complaints.I know everyone has a different experience when they stay at a hotel, and everyone has their own expectations, requirements, etc. I'm just writing this review because I had a pretty good experience, and I don't want others to be misled by all the bad reviews on here. One further note ... We were traveling with a group of around 80 people, and I've still not heard any complaints about their rooms or their hotel experience. Their experiences and opinions seemed to parallel ours.

<Content>Theft at the Condado We checked into the Condado for one night before heading to the south side of the island for a week. Room service was aware of our intentions of leaving the room. Perfect opportunity. They assume if you're leaving the next day, chances are you're not going to unpack completely and by the time you realize something's missing - you're probably home already and your bags have been through the airport, etc. making it difficult to know where the theft occured. It was the start of our trip so we hung around and filed a police report. I wonder how prevelant this practice is. You'd expect a Hotel like the Condado, with a casino esp., to have serious security in place but they obviously don't. We asked to see a record of keycard entry for our room or video from the halls and they refused obviously. A security guard in the lobby told us that their hiring practices were so poor it doubles thier work load. They not only have to look out for shady guests, it's the staff that's frightening. At 3 p.m. we waited in line another twenty minutes to finally get a room on the 9th floor of the tower which smelled much like cat urine. There were obviously much needed renovations in progress. We visited the casino, where we couldn't even get on the roulette table. There were crowds of people surrounding the two open tables, and yet between the six dealers mulling around behind the tables, they still didn't open up either of the two other tables. We were charged $6 for a Coors Light at the casino bar, and when inquiring as to the exorbitant price, the bartender sarcastically said, Welcome to Condado.I actually booked this room through Hotwire, and was told that what I paid included taxes. But upon check out, found that we were charged an additional $18 in taxes and tariffs. I was extremely disappointed in the condition of the hotel and our floor and the service I received from staff. Although I am not a By Request member, I spent several weeks at the Wyndham in Los Angeles, which was by far superior in quality and service. Should I ever know anyone misfortunate enough to visit Puerto Rico, The Wyndham Condado will not be my recommendation.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wyndam Condado Plaza We just returned from a 5 day, four night stay at the Wyndham Condado Plaza and thought we would write a quick review. The hotel was ok... just ok. It wasn't terrible, but definitely not a 4 star hotel. The room was nice; we had an oceanview which was the best part of staying there. The rooms do need a carpet upgrade but that's pretty typical of ocean front hotels. Not too bad but stained in some areas and you can tell it has been there a while. The maid service was excellent though.The restaurants looked nice, a little pricy but since we wanted to experience the culture and not Tony Romas like we have here in Ohio, we ventured out to eat. There is a nice coffee shop outside though by the valet parking that has muffins and danish for 2$ each. Nice value for breakfast when combined with the free coffee in the rooms.The Casino was nothing to write home about. They advertise it as the best in PR but we walked to the Raddison and even the Diamond Palace Hotel and found better games and machines that worked. It was a 20 minute walk and we had fun people watching while we were walking, if you like that sort of thing. The tables at Wyndam are mainly BlackJack, no Let it Ride or 3 Card Poker like they advertise so don't expect it. Also, many of their machines don't take bills and honestly, they were tight as a drum. We had more luck down the street. Even though the casinos down the street were better, if you are going on a gambling vacation, stick to Vegas, you'll win more and be able to play longer on your bankroll.The pools were nice and not crowded. We're not really into the beach scene so the fact that the beach was small and not directly on the ocean (it was located on an inlet with not many waves or anything except street people trying to sell you coconuts!) we didn't mind.If you are there for just a few nights during a cruise or something, I suppose this hotel is doable, but if you want to really experience a fine hotel and the culture, stay at the Marriott or Raddison down the street.Final note: We went to the Bahamas last year and read reviews on here saying the people of the island are rude to tourists. Not true! They were all pleasant and helpful. We read the same thing about Puerto Rico and thought nothing of it until we arrived. I got the feeling they are tired of the tourists. Not quite as friendly even when you go overboard to be nice to them. We won't be going back so I guess they don't have to worry!

<Content>Hotel nice - Staff not helpful Just got back from the Wyndham Condado Plaza - what an experience. We happened to be there during Tropical Storm Jeanne. I will say that the hotel was nice, room was better than we expected and until the storm hit everything was fine - except our whirlpool tub didn't work (called every day and no one responded). To start with, no one from the hotel gave us any information on the upcoming storm and since the news was in spanish we didn't figure it out until it was obvious. We saw a sign posted at the casino that they were closing due to the approaching storm but were assured by the security guard that we would be fine, just rained out. About 12:00 noon on Wednesday, just as we ordered our lunch the power went out so we were told we could not get lunch. After heading back to our dark room we watched as pieces of the roof and building started to blow away. Finally someone from the hotel knocked on the door and told us we had to vacate the room and come to the mezanine level - along with the rest of the guests, to sit in the dark. We were offered peanut butter or tuna fish sandwiches and soft drinks, until they ran out - then nothing. We were finally allowed back into our very dark rooms that night to sleep with no A/C or lights only to wake the next morning to the offer of a $6 continental breakfast, $1 coffee and $2 water - what a joke. We left the hotel, walked a block to the Hacienda restaurant to find a full hot breakfast with juice and coffee for $5.50 - they were great! During the whole ordeal the staff was completely unhelpful, provided no information and was unwilling to make any accomodations for the guests. Had we not had such a terrible response from the staff we would visit again but their attitude spoiled our trip and put us off for any future visits. Just a note - the ocean is beautiful to look at from the hotel but completley inaccessible. Certainly not worthy of being called a beach. Wyndham took advantage of a very scarey situation, price gouging for food was most uncalled for and certainly not good customer service. We opted to sit in the airport for six hours rather than stay there another minute.

There were a lot of kids on it, but I tried it out and it was great. I went everyday, it was a very nice short walk.One thing I have to tell you is to stay away from one of the restaurants in the hotel, Max's grill. $20 for a plate of food. Don't even bother eating there, unless if you have that kind of money. Right next door is an Italian restaurant where they have good food for a decent price. Overall I was very satisfied with the hotel, so satisfied that I'm staying there again next year. Don鈥檛 listen to the negative comments like I did. Some people are just too high maintenance and are expecting Trump Towers or something like the ritz, you get what you paid for, and I got what I paid for and more. See it for yourself, instead of reading the reviews, it's worth a weekend stay.
