<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hey tourists, this is a good place to stay I was terrified after reading the previous reviews. However, pleasantly surprised at all the smiles I received upon check in and during my stay. The staff is very friendly--but you must be respectful and friendly as well. Puerto Ricans do not respond well to egotistical behavior. Hotel is beautiful and is being remodeled. I did not mind the fresh paint scent in some areas. BEWARE OF THE HIGH FOOD PRICES AT THIS HOTEL. Do not eat here unless you are very wealthy. Go outside your hotel to Ashford Ave (to the left of the front entrance of the main building). You will find great breakfasts for less than $6.00 and ocean view. For dinner, again, try the local restaurants like Ropa Vieja and Ajili Mojili. They are expensive, but the food is sooo much better than Max's Grill. BEWARE Pina Coladas at the hotel are from instant mixes (YUCK). Ask for the real thing--coconut milk and pineapple juice. Do Ride the bus to Old San Juan and be ready for homeless folks to ask for money. Say NO and walk away. If you stop they will follow you and annoy you. They are not dangerous. There is a lot of security in the area. Join Wyndham by Request for the best rooms available and walk about ten minutes to the nearest beach, which is condado beach. A bit rough for little ones, but great for boogy boards. You can purchase boogy boards at Walgreens, just across the street. The beach at the hotel has many Sea Orchens (did I spell this right) and can be a nuisance. Not a good place to swim--snorkeling for adults is okay. Overall---a more than good experience. This hotel is a great place to stay. Casino open 24 hours and live music until 2 am. Go ahead and book your room, and have a great time. I sure did!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't listen to the bad reviews of this hotel! I'm not sure what everyone is complaining about related to this hotel -- don't have a second thought about staying at the Wyndham Condado Plaza! We were almost swayed not to stay there due to the negative comments on Trip Advisor, but the deal we got through Priceline was too good to pass up. Every moment of our stay there (July 23-28, 2004) was amazing. We arrived about 12 hours later than expected due to flight delays, and our luggage was lost. The hotel staff made check-in a breeze, and housekeeping provided us with necessary toiletries immediately to replace what we were without. We were blown away by our room -- despite the fact that we booked through a discounter, we had THE BEST room in the entire hotel. We were placed on the 10th floor Plaza Club. Our enormous room had a couch and armchair, desk, Aeron chair, mini-fridge, TV armoire, dimmer lights, a king-sized bed, a walk-in closet for our luggage (once it arrived!), and a gleaming bathroom. The view of the Condado Lagoon from our room was spectacular. The location of the Wyndham Condado Plaza is ideal -- Condado is a safe and pretty neighborhood. There are lots of restaurants right on Ashford (the street the hotel is on) and there's on-site parking underneath the hotel with a very affordable daily rate. You have easy access to Old San Juan (a short taxi ride away), Luiz Munoz Marin Airport is less than a half-hour trip, and it's a quick drive to major highways if you're renting a car to get to other parts of the island. The hotel has two pools -- a salt pool and a chlorine pool with a swim-up cabana bar. It's literally 100 feet to the beach from the hotel, which is right on the Condado Lagoon -- we went snorkeling on the reef right in front of the hotel! There are excellent restaurants right in the hotel (the Italian place on the mezzanine level was our favorite), and we loved the room service -- the food quality was excellent and it arrived quickly. The hotel staff were helpful and super nice. In short, we would stay there again in a heartbeat.

Go to Old San Juan by taxi and eat at the Parrot Club. You'll love the food and lively atmosphere. El Yunque is a must-see and wear your swimsuit under your clothes to experience the lovely waterfalls. Enjoy the live music at the hotel, especially on weekends. Upon checkout, look at your bill very carefully! They overbilled us for 2 restaurants that we never ate at, but it was later corrected and apologies were made. Overall, the hotel was nice, but lacking in its locale to the beach and in its not so helpful and competent staff.

<Content>Good spot to stay at in San Juan I am a local, but my family loves to do internal tourism. I have stayed twice at the Condado Plaza, but have visited the hotel too many times. In the Old San Juan the hot spot is in San Sebastian or down closer to the bay near Teatro Tapia. In Isla Verde the most popular place to go is Babylon (it's a discotheque). Tourism spots which are good obviously the Old San Juan and there is also El Yunque which is rain forest 45min away from San Juan. Also if you like shopping (American Style)...you should take a cab and go to Plaza Las Americas which is the biggest shopping mall in the Caribbean.

<Content>Too Expensive I stayed at this hotel for 5 days and 4 nights. I arrived with trepidation because of the previous reviews that I read about this hotel. I thought that the process was absurd. This hotel is huge and it needs to have more check-in/out staff to accommodate the mass influx/exit of guests. I wasn't impressed with the reception desk staff who were aloof, as were the people who gave you towels at the pool and the wait staff in the high-end restaurant. The wait staff where the buffet was served were wonderful, though. I wasn't impressed with the beach at all. It had trash and debris all over the sand and it was absolutely tiny. I will be going back to beautiful Puerto Rico,but I will be staying at another hotel. I would not recommend this hotel to anyone, as it is way too expensive for all the problems that it has.

<Content>What to Expect We stayed at this hotel from May 10-14th, 2004. The most important thing to note about this hotel is that the website, etc. is incredibly misleading. Here is the deal. <Author>Milt07
<Content>Notl like it was This was the second time that I stayed at The Condado Plaza and quite frankly, it seems to be a shell of its former self. The hotel is still lovely, but it is beginning to show its age. The marble floors in the lobby are showing spots of heavy wear and tear. The huge aquarium is a nice touch, but the spacing of the nite club proximity is too close to the telephones. I was trying to make a phone call, and I couldn't hear. I arrived at the hotel on April 29, 2004 around 12:00 p.m. and my room was not ready. I belong to the Wyndham by Request and had requested an oceanview room. I did not get into my room until 3:15 p.m. after several trips to the front desk. They did offer to upgrade me to the Plaza level, however, there were no more oceanview suites. They did offer to put me on the lagoon side, but I opted for the full breakfast buffet vouchers instead. The plaza level comes with a deluxe continental breakfast, but it is not better than the buffet especially for someone with a healthy appetite like myself. The room was nice with a oceanview that was incredible. I could see cruise ships at night on the horizon and parasailing and jetskiing during the day. The breeze never ceased and I slept with the balcony door open every night.The bathroom amenities were more than you ask for. The only problem with the bathroom was when you took a shower, it took a long timefor the water to leave the tub. I did not want to go thru the hassle of asking for another room as I fell in love with the view, so I just imagined I had my feet in the water at the beach. This was a minor problem and did not affect my trip. Speaking of the beach, they have a small one on the side of the hotel, but it is a public beach and the take advantage of it. There is a path to the beach from the gorgeous pool area with security stationed at the entrance to keep anyone who is not a guest from entering the property unless they are with you of course. They have three pools at the hotel, one on the lagoon side and two on the main side. The saltwater pool is 6ft deep , the regular pool is approx 4ft deep with a volleyball net , water slide, and swim up bar. There is a jacuzzi which is nice. All the pools are open 24 hours, so enjoy! The jacuzzi gets a little busy late at night as the weather has cooled off a bit. In the midst of the pools is Las Palmas, a restaurant with reasonably priced snacks and lite meals. It is open and has nice breezes blowing all the time. The swim up bar closes at 12:00 am. There is a separate pool elevator available to guests that they prefer you use from the evening on as they have a certain atmosphere they try to maintain. No swimsuits in the lobby at night. They would prefer use wear slacks for men and appropiate evening wear for the ladies. They are not stuffy but want you dress a little bit at night ( not formal ). The hotel has six restaurants from a deli to a onsite Tony Roma's. The buffet is served at Max's and is not cheap, I had vouchers so I really could not tell you how much it was, but I did hear my friends say between 10 and 15. There is a nice place a few doors down from the hotel that has a great breakfast special for $5.50. The hotel concierge has all the info on the tours which range from 30 - 100.00 . My advice to you is rent a car for at least one day across the street at Charlies and do Puerto Rico your way. Also, I noticed a faint smell of mildew on the hallway carpets which seems to be a problem with a lot of hotels in the carribean. I wish they all had tiles. These are minor things and should not stop you from staying at the Condado.

Again, this is good if you have children and don't want to worry about them in the surf, etc. Our son (11 yrs old) actually did a little snorkeling and enjoyed it. At the back of the hotel is a sea wall with the rocks in all. We ate breakfast outside on the patio with a beautiful view of the waves crashing into the rocks, palm trees, etc. It was very nice. They also have a casino which was very busy. The staff there are very pleasant and helpful. We had a situation where the bellman dropped a box of duty free liquor we had purchased on our cruise however besides being extremely apologetic, he and the manager drove all over town to replace the bottles that broke. They really made every attempt to correct the situation. I would recommend this hotel especially to families. We would enjoyed our short stay and would definetly stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We were happy with our stay here... We stayed at the Condado for 4 nights, before going to Fajardo. The hotel room was pleasant, though a little dated. The room had 2 double beds, and huge walk-in closet. My daughter was sick for 2 days, and my son decided to sleep in the closet - and it was plenty big enough to do so. We had joined Wyndham By Request, so we were upgraded to an ocean-view room (beautiful view!) and given beer, water and cheese  crackers upon our arrival. The pools were beautiful, and not very crowded. No worry about getting a chair. Because I read the reviews here, I was not expecting much of a beach. The beach is small, but is actually nicer than I had anticipated. It is right next to the pool area, so you can go back and forth easily and without leaving the property. We did venture out into town to eat a few times, which I would recommend. Ropa Viejo was a nice restaurant with local flair. The mojitos here are the best we had on the islands. The ceviche was terrific too. Also, go the the restaurant next door El Wakkiki for breakfast. $5 for eggs, pancakes or huevos rancheros (with homemade guac  salsa!) and overlooks the ocean. The best meal we had here was at Ramiro's. It is pricey, but no more so than eating at the hotel. The food was FANTASTIC!! We are food/wine people, and are very picky. This restaurant was one of the best anywhere, and the service was terrific. Definitely worth the trip! As for food at the hotel, stay away from Max's, except maybe for lunch. The spanish restaurant was pretty good, we sat next to the fish tank and the food was decent. As far as trips go, don't do the tour of Old San Juan. You are better off just taking a cab into the city (about $10) and walking around. Great little shops, good restaurants  night life. The fort is great, and huge! If you go on the tour they only give you 1/2 hour to see the fort, which is not nearly enough. Overall, we really enjoyed our time in San Juan and the Wyndham Condado was a good choice for us.

<Content>Good hotel...just forget the beach part of it Just returned from a 5 night stay at the Condado Plaza. Honestly, if being on the beach is the main thing, then try the Marriott or the hotels in Isla Verde. If not, the Wyndham is fine.

Upon arrival, there were some minor problems with our reservations (did not have my by request with reservations and wrong room type), but this was remedies quickly as they upgraded us to an ocean front view. The view was incredible and we had a very large balcony (many rooms had next to nothing for balconies). The walk in closet was spacious enough for a person to change in while someone else occupied the bathroom. Very helpful for teens!! If you are a beach person, stay somewhere else as the beach was quite dismal. However, the pool area and grounds were very nice for relaxing and enjoying the troical scenery. 1 day at the pools and beach is enough, get out and see Old San Juan or take a trip to Fahardo for snorkling or to see the rain forrest.There were some minor problems with room service not getting orders correct, but it didn't make the vacation a wash-out. Police seem to be everywhere around the Condado area and walking to various places felt very safe. THere are many restaurants close by and the walk in the evenings was quite nice.Overall, a very nice vacation with clean rooms and ok service. I give it an A and will go back again!

<Content>nothing special, very ordinary Definitely not a four diamond/star hotel.Positives: Nice lobby, beautiful grounds (3 pools, overlooking the ocean), beach was very small, but okay. If you are a beach person you might want to stay further down on the strip or in isla verda. At night we walked along Ashford avenue, which was very nice, very safe to do. We joined Wyndham by Request (no charge) and got upgraded to an ocean view room. The rooms were very spacious and had huge walk in closets. There was nightly entertainment, 24 hour casino and tons of places to eat on site. Bus stop is located right beside the hotel and takes you right into old san juan for 25 cents. Pleasant hotel staff/good service.The Negatives include: The furniture in the room was a bit on the shabby side ( some scratches, dents, rust on wall lamps)and the carpet was worn. Cracked tile in the bathrooms which felt outdated. We were part of a large party staying at the hotel, so we got to see other rooms, and these were the same - nothing special, great view but with slightly shabby outdated furniture. Gym use was $7 per day.This hotel would be a perfect place to stay if the rooms were nicer and the beach were better. Overall though, as it is, it is very ordinary.

<Author>wellsfargo
<Content>Not bad My wife and I spent our honeymoon in San Juan and stayed at this resort. We got this place through Priceline. After reading the reviews from this website, we were very concerned about staying hers. There are so many negative things that were mentioned. Prior to arriving, I called Wyndham and shared my concerns about their hotel. I also contacted PriceLine and told them the same things. We are Wyndham by Request members. When we arrived at the hotel, we were greeted promptly by the front desk staff. They told us that our room was ready on the 10th floor which is the Club Plaza. When we got to the top, we were greeted by the conciere. He told us that we had the Presidential Suite and that a bottle of wine and cheese were waiting on us. There is only one Presidential Suite and it goes for over 1000 in the off season and 2000 in peak season. When we went to our room, we were very pleased with the accomadations. There were two seperate bathrooms, all marble tile, jetted over sized tub and a very large bedroom. We couldn't believe that we were upgraded to this room. Only thought that we had was that Wyndham wanted to make it right because of our phone call and concerns. Every night in the Club Lounge there were appetizers and in the morning there was a continental breakfast. The staff treated us like royalty the whole time. The room was very clean. We ate at Maxis one time and the service was prompt and the food was great. The casino was fine and it was not that crowded and we even won some money the last night. The pool was fine, but it could be deeper. The beach off of the hotel is nothing to shout about. If your looking for a beach, this place is not for you. However, there are plenty of quality restaurants close by. Old San Juan is less than five minutes by taxi. The taxi fares are negotiable and not set in stone. There are police everywhere and it is very safe to walk the streets around the hotel. We would recommend you stay here for the right price and get a room on the ocean side. There are two buildings. Don't stay in the building above Tony Romas, you have no views. Hope this helps

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>OK hotel - but find someplace else to eat! Over the winter school break we flew into San Juan on JetBlue (wonderful airline) from JFK in NY. At JFK, we left our car with AviStar, an off-airport parking service. This was a great idea. They provided a shuttle service to the terminal, and it was cheaper than parking in the airport lot. When we returned, they picked us up and put our luggage into our waiting, heated car!Upon arrival in PR, it cost us about $15 for three of us plus luggage to take a cab to the hotel (no free shuttle service). The cab ride was about twenty minutes or so. Check in took five minutes.Our room was ready when we arrived and we were fortunate enough to get upgraded from a city view to an ocean view. Hint - join Wyndham by Request when you call to make your reservation- there is no charge. Book the cheaper room and request an upgrade if one is available when you make the reservation and also when you check in. The Condado Plaza has two towers the one we stayed at overlooked the ocean and had the lobby and the majority of restaurants. The other tower overlooks the lagoon and the city of San Juan.The room was lovely. It was very large and clean. The entrance hallway had a credenza unit with a fairly large refrigerator inside and a pretty nice sized area for storing food (we called it the kitchen). On top of the unit was a complimentary basket with bottled water, crackers, cheese, a bottle of wine and some other goodies, courtesy of Wyndham by Request. There was also a small coffeemaker with samples of Puerto Rican coffee for early risers. The bathroom was average sized with lots of counter space and room for toiletries. The sink was in the bathroom, not outside like in some hotels. No problem with hot water or water pressure.There was a VERY large walk-in closet adjacent to the bathroom. It may have even been larger than the bathroom. I have never seen such a large closet in any hotel I have been to. You could probably have a couple of small kids sleep in this rr all of our hanging clothing and suitcases. The minibar, which we never used, was in this room.Our room had two queen beds, two large chairs and lamps for reading, a desk with two desk chairs, and an armoire with a large TV and VCR inside. (Video tapes are available for rent from the hotel).There was a balcony overlooking the ocean with a small plastic resin table and two chairs. The door out to the balcony looked brand new. We had absolutely no problems with housekeeping the week we were there. We only spent a small amount of time in the casino. It was large compared to others we saw in Puerto Rico, but small compared to a recent visit to Las Vegas. It generally seemed to be crowded in the evening, but not cramped.The main pool was very nice it has a slide, which the kids enjoyed. There were numerous chairs and lounges everywhere with comfy cushions. We never had a problem getting a place to sit in the sun or the shade. You get pool towels from a booth as you enter the pool area. A bill for $10 per towel is written up and filed in a box. When you return the towels the receipt is ripped up. A novelty was that the pools were open 24 hours a day. One night we went swimming at midnight. There were always people (including security staff) walking around, so you felt safe.There is also a saltwater pool, which was interesting, and two hot tubs, which were just ok. (We have a spa at home, so were not overly impressed). The public beach is very small, practically on the road and not very appealing. We never went to that beach. Instead, we asked the concierge one morning to call one of their sister hotels, the Wyndham Old San Juan on Isla Verde. She arranged for us to use their facilities gratis, as we were registered guests. That was great. We took a $10 cab ride to that hotel which was really beautiful. We were given a wristband, which allowed us full use of the facilities including their much larger pool and beach area and towels. That was a fun afternoon.We spent a short time one evening in the hotel lobby people watmmense salt water aquarium. We also had drinks in two different lounges, one with a live band. Now, here are the negatives. We had problems with every one of the hotel restaurants we visited.Tony Romas is a casual rib place in the lagoon tower. We had a real communication problem with our waiter that took two other people to resolve. At check-in you are given a cardboard charge card to charge items to your room. We first used it at this restaurant, and it took almost 40 minutes just to get a receipt for our dinner. Needless to say, we did not use it again.Another night we went to Maxs Grill. Our waitress was sullen and unhappy and didnt seem to want to be there. The food was ok though. Prices were high, but not more than one would expect at an urban hotel.The worst was our visit to Cobia. This is their deluxe seafood restaurant. (A la Carte, with entrees in the $25+ range). We planned on making this a memorable vacation evening. Well, we were seated at our table and ignored, as tables around us were served. After about 30 minutes, we left.Not one person a waiter, busperson, hostess, etc., came by to offer us a menu, a drink, or even some water or bread. Certainly not the kind of service to expect in an expensive restaurant in a nice hotel. By the way, the restaurant was half empty and this was a weeknight, so I dont think an overworked staff was the problem.To sum it up, the hotel was ok, but eat elsewhere!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I loved Puerto Rico. Stay anywhere but go. Honestly I thought Puerto Rico was wonderful. The hotel was very nice without anything to complain about. The pool is beautiful. If you want to get a good spot you must get there early. The sun is not on the pool in the morning so save a chair with some belongings by the dolphin fountains by the steps of the pool. This is the area that gets the most sun during the day. The beach is small and kind of does suck, but when it is 10 degrees back home, who can knock it. I fully recommend the catarmaran snorkeling tour. They take you to a beautiful deserted island with a beautiful beach on the carribean side. The water is crystal clear and incredible. Exactly what you want. DO NOT book the tour to the rain forest. At the hotel it cost 35 a person. They take you there on a nature walk and don't let you near the waterfall. Rent a car and drive there so you can explore like I wish I had. Admission to the rainforest is 3 dollars a person. The thing that sucked about the hotel was the bs charges. I didn't mind the 7 dollar large bottle water I drank in the room except they charge a 20% restocking charge. So it was then 8.20. I think their profit margin is already high enough why add the 20%. Everything in the hotel has a 20% charge so be ready for it. Also, breakfast. You would think they would have something reasonable in the hotel. Nope. $15 for the continental and $18 for the buffet which included eggs and french toast. Besides these petty things and my $40 dollar breakfast with tip, I had a wonderful time. As for being the largest casino, don't think your in vegas or AC. It might be the largest for Puerto Rico but for anyone else it is smaller then the tiny outskirts of vegas casinos. Daytime play was fine but don't bother at night. Way too crowded. I have to admit. Next time I will pick a hotel in Isla Verde with a nicer beach.
